**§51.11.2 — The actuator is proven and ignited under fail-closed shadow.** **Slice 102** (PR #69299) is a hermetic soak proving the graduation engine *earns* and executes a master flip from telemetry while the **Tiered Authority** boundary holds (STANDARD cognitive substrates → AUTO_FLIP; SAFETY/governance flags → APPROVAL_ADVISORY, structurally refused at the override-ledger tier gate). **Slice 103** deploys **Production Shadow Mode**: `graduation_override_ledger.shadow_mode_enabled()` is **fail-closed default-TRUE** (only an explicit `JARVIS_GRADUATION_SHADOW_MODE=false` un-shadows; unset *or garbage* stays shadowed). In shadow, AUTO_FLIP receipts accrue to a separate shadow ledger the boot applier never reads — the engine generates evidence + receipts + SAFETY advisories but **never executes the OS-level flip.** The Sleep Daemon runs the engine off-hot-path. **The human remains the sole actuator** — this is the Tier-1→D bridge: the mechanism is built and provably safe; only real wall-clock evidence (and the operator's explicit un-shadow) authorizes a flip. *(Remaining operational step: register the cognitive substrates in the cadence policy + wire a clean-session recorder so their evidence accrues — onboarding, not engineering.)*

**§51.11.3 — The redefined frontier (supersedes §51.7 Tier 2 ordering).** With Tier 1 closed and the actuator safe, the **two highest-priority engineering hurdles to Tier D** — both mapping to §43 and aligned with **Anthropic's ASL framework / scalable-oversight** research — are now the critical path:

1. **OS-Level Runtime Containment (§43 Arc 5) — eliminate the ~8.8% bypass.** The cage is static-analysis-complete but cannot catch `eval`/`exec`/`subprocess`/`pickle` of *runtime-constructed* values (the §41.11.2 residual). The fix is **OS-level** — seccomp-bpf syscall filtering + Linux namespaces (or a Docker/gVisor sandbox profile) wrapping the APPLY/VERIFY execution boundary. This is the **only unconditional containment guarantee** and the precondition for any operator-out-of-loop ("O+V develops Trinity") claim. Maps to ASL-4 deployment-containment expectations (RSP v3.0).
2. **Operator-Independent Recursion-Depth Counter (RRD §23.5 / §43).** Today the *operator* is the recursion bound — the governance boundary gate prevents autonomous *application* of cage changes but is advisory if the operator is out-of-loop. Tier D requires a **mathematical** bound: a durable per-cycle counter of governance-touching modifications with a hard HALT ceiling, decoupled from any application-state ledger (the watchdog-isolation invariant). This is the structural prerequisite for **Order-2 RSI** (O+V rewriting its own cognition) without unbounded regress — the formal core of the "Thermodynamic Containment of Agentic Entropy" dissertation thesis (extending Wang arXiv:1805.06610).

**Honest verdict (unchanged in spirit, sharpened in fact):** the engineering frontier has moved *up* — Bucket A (the easy ~15%) is essentially done; the organism now learns, consolidates, self-audits, and proactively explores, and can demonstrably ignite itself **safely**. What remains between here and Tier D is exactly the hard 85% §51 always named: **OS-level runtime containment + the operator-independent recursion bound + 12–18 months of real wall-clock evidence under shadow.** Fully-autonomous remains *earned, not flipped* — and the Slice 103 fail-closed actuator is the mechanism that guarantees it stays that way.

**§51.11.4 — Slice 104 (Tier 2 Containment Protocol, 2026-06-06): both hurdles attacked.** (1) **Operator-Independent Recursion-Depth Gate — BUILT + un-bypassable.** `recursion_depth_gate.py` upgrades the path-predicate into a mathematical depth bound: a process-singleton tracker counts consecutive governance-touching APPLYs (the self-modification chain "Order depth"), and when a chain would exceed `MAX_RECURSION_DEPTH` (default 3) the op is routed to the strictest `blocked` tier via `risk_tier_floor._recursion_depth_floor` — severing a runaway self-mod loop autonomously, no human in the loop. Default-TRUE safety gate; wired at the orchestrator APPLY terminal seam. This is hurdle #2, **done** (the structural prerequisite for safe Order-2 RSI). (2) **OS-Level Runtime Containment — primitive built, honest platform split.** `runtime_sandbox.py` runs generated code in a SEPARATE confined OS process (stripped env, cwd→worktree, `resource` rlimits, hard-timeout→SIGKILL) — on the macOS/arm64 dev host these blast-radius guarantees are real + adversarially TESTED (rogue env-exfiltration foiled, infinite loop killed, zero parent leakage); the strong kernel guarantees (seccomp-bpf syscall filter, namespace isolation, network-egress denial, absolute-FS confinement) are a Linux/GCP **injectable backend interface** that this host cannot run — explicitly NOT claimed active here (`guarantees_for_platform` returns the truthful per-platform list). Master default-FALSE; the primitive ships with its adversarial proof but is **not yet wired into the live APPLY/VERIFY path** — that wiring + the real Linux seccomp backend are the remaining steps to close the ~8.8% residual on production (Linux) hosts. Honest status: hurdle #1 is **scaffolded + proven for its testable guarantees**, with the kernel-sandbox activation correctly deferred to a Linux host.

**§51.11.5 — Slice 105 (Linux/Docker Containment Bridge, 2026-06-06): hurdle #1's kernel path is now locally runnable.** Docker Desktop on macOS/arm64 runs a REAL Linux kernel in a lightweight VM, so a hardened Docker container delivers genuine KERNEL containment with the IDENTICAL profile production runs on GCP/Linux — Docker is the bridge from the dev Mac to the Tier-D containment model (no GCP host required to verify). `container_sandbox.py` is the general-purpose `ContainerizedSandboxBackend`: it COMPOSES Slice 92's already-proven zero-trust profile (`container_engine.build_hardened_security_argv` — `--cap-drop ALL` + `--network none` + `--security-opt no-new-privileges` + `--read-only` + `--pids-limit` + non-exec tmpfs, written precisely to neutralize the 5 residual `run_body_*` runtime sinks) with Slice 104's `ContainmentResult`/`ContainmentBreach` types, so ARBITRARY generated APPLY/VERIFY code is injected into the locked-down container, executed async (the injectable `_real_docker_run` IPC bridge), and stdout/stderr pulled back; a contained sink may execute but cannot exfiltrate / reach host FS / escalate / fork-bomb. `run_payload_contained` is the gated live-wire surface (returns `None` when off → legacy; a `ContainmentResult` when on → caller records a `ContainmentBreach` + falls back gracefully). A strict opt-in seccomp profile ships (`sandbox_profiles/strict_runtime.seccomp.json`, default-allow + 29-syscall host-escape deny-list, defense-in-depth). 11 mock tests (deterministic, no Docker) + 1 real-Docker integration test (network-egress-denial proof, skipped on the dev host, runs on any Docker host). HONEST remaining: the one-line adoption at the orchestrator VERIFY seam + a real-Docker soak (Docker wasn't running this dev session) — but the kernel-containment mechanism is now built, composed from battle-tested parts, and locally verifiable the moment a Docker daemon is up. The ~8.8% residual is now **closeable on any Linux/Docker host**, not just GCP.

**§51.11.6 — Slice 106 (Empirical Containment Receipt + FSM wiring, 2026-06-06): the cage HOLDS under live fire, and is wired into VERIFY.** The Docker daemon was booted and the containment was proven against the REAL Linux kernel (Docker 29.5.2 on M1/arm64), captured as a permanent gated regression test (`tests/architecture/test_slice106_live_containment.py`, runs live when Docker is up):

> **RECEIPT (live):** a malicious payload EXECUTED inside the hardened container but `net=EGRESS_BLOCKED` (`--network none`), `etc=ETC_WRITE_BLOCKED` + `root=ROOT_WRITE_BLOCKED` (`--read-only` rootfs), `work=WORK_WRITE_OK` (the worktree mount is the sole writable host path), an infinite loop was timeout-killed (TIMEOUT breach @4s), and the parent process never crashed. The 8.8%-class runtime sink is empirically contained.

FSM wiring: `run_payload_contained` is now wired into the orchestrator VERIFY phase as a **gated, additive, fail-safe** hook — when `JARVIS_RUNTIME_SANDBOX_ENABLED` is on AND a containment probe (`JARVIS_RUNTIME_SANDBOX_VERIFY_PROBE`) is configured, the candidate's runtime validation runs in the locked-down container; a `ContainmentBreach` (timeout / signal-kill / nonzero) marks VERIFY failed (reusing the EXISTING failure → L2/GENERATE_RETRY routing) and records a FALSIFYING **quarantine belief** (`container_sandbox.record_containment_breach_belief`) so the Phase-3 learning loop + Phase-6 consolidation steer GENERATE away from the breaching paradigm. The breach NEVER crashes the FSM (the gate is fully `try/except`-wrapped). Default-FALSE → byte-identical legacy. HONEST remaining: containerizing the FULL project test suite needs a project image (the generic `python:3.11-slim` lacks the repo's deps) + a production soak — that's the deployment step; the containment mechanism, the breach→quarantine path, and the gated wire are built, live-proven, and tested. **Hurdle #1 (OS-Level Runtime Containment) is now empirically demonstrated and FSM-integrated; the remaining work is operational (project image + soak), not architectural.**

**§51.11.7 — Slice 107 (Ephemeral Project Container pipeline, 2026-06-06): the deployment pipeline is built + live-proven.** Three pieces, all verified against the live Docker daemon: (1) an **elite multi-stage, multi-arch Dockerfile** (`sandbox_profiles/Dockerfile.verify-sandbox` + `requirements-sandbox.txt`) — the image carries ONLY the pytest stack (project code mounted read-only at run time, heavy ML deps NOT baked), so it cold-boots fast (built locally at 56 MB / 5.6 s) and supports `linux/arm64` (M1) + `linux/amd64` (GCP); (2) an **async Image Provisioning Daemon** (`image_provisioner.py`) — hashes `requirements-sandbox.txt` + the Dockerfile into an image label, rebuilds in the background only when stale, non-blocking, idempotent (live-proven: rebuilt-then-current); (3) **real pytest-in-container** (`container_sandbox.run_pytest_in_container` + a general pytest-summary parser) — runs the suite against the read-only worktree mount in the hardened image and returns structured pass/fail telemetry to feed the belief loop (live-proven: `2 passed, 1 failed, 3 total`, failure named). A **Shadow Soak Runbook** (`docs/operations/shadow_soak_runbook.md`) gives the exact commands to launch full Shadow Mode (Entropy Engine + Sleep Daemon + Sandbox + fail-closed graduation) for wall-clock evidence accrual. 12 tests (mock matrix + live Docker). HONEST: the FULL governance suite in-container still needs a **project image** with the import-chain deps (`backend.core.ouroboros.__init__` eager-imports aiohttp + the engine chain) — documented in the runbook; the light image + the whole pipeline (build / provision / pytest-in-container / parse) are built + live-verified. **The Tier-D runtime cage is now deployment-ready: build / provision / contain / verify, end-to-end on Docker.**

**§51.11.8 — Slice 108 (Production layer-cached container, 2026-06-06): the TRUE O+V suite runs contained — live-proven.** §51.11.7's "FULL suite needs a project image" was the open gap; Slice 108 closes it with a key empirical finding (a `sys.modules` probe, not a guess): `import backend.core.ouroboros.governance.*` pulls a MEDIUM dependency closure — aiohttp + cryptography + networkx + redis + opentelemetry + psutil + yaml + ~10 more — and **NOT torch / whisper / transformers / numpy / scipy** (those are vision/voice-only). So the governance/self-development VERIFY image is **moderate, not multi-GB**. Delivered: (1) `Dockerfile.production-sandbox` + `requirements-governance.txt` — an elite layer-cached, multi-stage, multi-arch image enforcing the **Immutability Invariant** (heavy deps in an immutably-cached layer keyed ONLY on the requirements file; the volatile source is NEVER baked — the live worktree is volume-mounted read-only, so a single-file mutation triggers ZERO rebuild). BuildKit pip cache-mount; parameterizable `ARG REQUIREMENTS` (governance default, or the full-ML `requirements.txt` for vision/voice). Built live at **72 MB in 11 s**. (2) The `image_provisioner` is now image-agnostic (hashes the CONFIGURED requirements + Dockerfile → rebuilds only on dep change; live-proven pre-warm of the production image). (3) `launch_shadow_soak.sh` — the final executable: boots Docker, builds-only-if-stale the layer-cached image, ignites the cognitive bus + substrates, and launches O+V into fail-closed Shadow Mode. **MARQUEE (live): the REAL O+V governance suite (`test_slice101_phase5_proof_gate`, 12 tests, importing the full governance chain) PASSED inside the hardened `--network none` / `--read-only` / `--cap-drop ALL` production container against the read-only worktree mount — no rebuild.** 5 tests (mock + live). **Both Tier-D hurdles are now mechanism-complete, FSM-integrated, AND the true suite runs contained in a layer-cached production image. The remaining path is purely the 12–18-month shadow wall-clock evidence — a clock, not code.**

**§51.11.9 — Slice 109 (God-Tier Observability Matrix & Voice Ignition, 2026-06-06): the §7 "absolute observability" surface for the cognitive organism.** With the nervous system wired (Slice 101), the actuator proven + shadowed (102/103), and the runtime cage live + contained (104→108), the last gap before the soak was *legibility*: the cognitive bus reasoned in private. Slice 109 adds a **decoupled telemetry router** (`cognitive_observability.py`) that subscribes to the Slice-101 lifecycle stream and fans every event to two authority-free sinks — composing the existing cognitive bus + SSE broker + DaemonNarrator, no new broker. (1) **The structured "Why-Snapshot"** (schema `cognitive_why_snapshot.v1`, new SSE event `EVENT_TYPE_COGNITIVE_WHY_SNAPSHOT`): on every `post_apply` / `post_failure` the FSM publish is enriched with the decision context (confidence + risk tier), and the router composes the live `confidence_aura` band, the `shannon_entropy` of the domain distribution, the `decision_prior_distribution` (belief-verdict histogram), `recursion_depth`, and any `rehearsal_verdict` into ONE JSON object the TUI / VS Code extension renders as time-travel debugging ("why did O+V believe what it believed, at the moment it decided?"). A bounded in-process ledger (`why_snapshot_for_op` / `recent_why_snapshots`) holds the recent snapshots for the dashboard. (2) **Karen's voice, ignited + wired to the bus.** A second subscriber narrates HIGH-severity cognitive events only (containment breach / graduation-threshold-met / load-shedding / failure) through the existing `DaemonNarrator` (new cognitive templates), dynamically formatted from the lifecycle payload. The gate ordering is **load-bearing and fail-closed**: master flag (`JARVIS_KAREN_VOICE_ENABLED`, §33.1 default-FALSE) → live mute state (read from `KarenConfig`; **if the config can't be read, Karen stays silent**) → severity. No TTS is ever queued unless all three pass; `say "Karen mute"` silences her live. macOS `say` needs an audio device, not a TTY, so the voice works in the headless soak; the *visual* TUI needs a TTY (`SHADOW_INTERACTIVE=1` drops `--headless` for an operator ignition session). Registered at GLS boot alongside the Slice-101 subscribers; both inert when the cognitive bus is off. **27 deterministic mock tests** (`tests/architecture/test_slice109_observability.py`) intercept the SSE publish + inject a recording narrator to prove the JSON shape and the gate logic with zero TTY/audio dependency. `launch_shadow_soak.sh` now exports the full observability + voice env. HONEST boundary: the visual TUI render + Karen's audible narration are **local operator verifications on a TTY + audio device** — this slice wires + proves the data-flow and gating; the human runs the launch and confirms the senses. **The organism is now fully legible: every autonomous decision broadcasts its reasoning over SSE and speaks its high-severity moments aloud. The soak is launch-ready.**

**§51.11.10 — Slice 110 (Native React/FastAPI Command Center, 2026-06-06): the sovereign interface — composed, not duplicated.** A Tier-D autonomous developer deserves a native real-time command center rather than terminal logs + an external IDE extension. **Verify-first found that three of the four literal build-steps would have duplicated existing infrastructure**: `backend/main.py` is already a `FastAPI()` app; `backend/api/broadcast_router.py` is already a typed FastAPI **WebSocket manager**; and `frontend/` is already a **React 19** CRA app (framer-motion + lucide-react + a zero-hardcode `config.js` + a full WS-client layer). The ONE genuinely-missing nerve — nothing bridged the internal `TrinityEventBus` / Slice-109 Why-Snapshots to the frontend — is the additive core. Delivered: (1) `backend/api/observability_gateway.py` — a **composing gateway** (FastAPI `APIRouter` mounted into the existing app, reusing the existing `BroadcastConnectionManager` class on a dedicated channel) exposing typed `gateway_frame.v1` frames over WebSocket (`/api/observability/ws`) + REST (`/health`, `/why-snapshots`, `/causality`). Its **bus→WS bridge** reuses the Slice-101 subscriber registry + Slice-109 Why-Snapshot builder (no recomputation, no duplicate schema), registered at GLS boot. (2) A React **Sovereign Command Center** (`frontend/src/components/CommandCenter/`) — a dependency-free SVG **force-directed Causality DAG** (ops + files; decision-flow + touches edges; no d3/new npm dep → clean lockfile), real-time **entropy + confidence-aura gauges** (framer-motion), a **live frame stream**, and a **cosmetic voice toggle** — mounted at `/command-center` via a minimal path switch in `index.js`. (3) `launch_shadow_soak.sh` gains a `COMMAND_CENTER=1` mode that boots Docker + the engine-hosting FastAPI backend + the React UI on `:3000` (alternative front-ends to the same engine — never double-booted). **Authority invariant (§1 sovereignty, fail-closed):** the gateway is **read-only over the web for everything authority-bearing**; the ONLY write surface is the *cosmetic* Karen mute/unmute, routed through the sanctioned `karen_voice_command_router` env seam and **loopback-only** — FSM state, governance flags, and graduation remain observable-but-not-mutable here (a browser endpoint that flipped authority would be a sovereignty leak past the Iron Gate). **18 deterministic integration tests** (`tests/architecture/test_slice110_command_center.py`) include the marquee state-synchronization assertion: a simulated FSM `ContainmentBreach` propagates through the bridge and arrives on a connected WS client as a high-severity `containment_breach` frame with the reverse-engineered breach vector — proven with FastAPI's `TestClient`, zero browser. HONEST boundary: the visual render at `localhost:3000`, the force-graph animation, and the "elite" aesthetic are **local operator verifications**; this slice wires + proves the data path that feeds them. **The nervous system now terminates in a native sovereign interface.**

### §51.11.A — The Tier-D Performance & GIL-Bypass Arc (Slices 111–114, 2026-06-06)

*A four-slice arc that turned the command center from a feature into a **structurally invincible** observability surface, by eliminating the single-event-loop coupling that let any GIL-heavy engine operation freeze the UI. Every slice in this arc had at least one literal premise overturned by verify-first against the live code — and the right thing was built instead of the requested thing. The arc closes with an **empirically-probed** result, not a claim.*

**§51.11.11 — Slice 111 (Core Optimization & Tech-Debt Eradication).** Two premises overturned. (1) **FlagRegistry debt was not "~10 callers" — it was 1000+ `register(name=, type_=, …)` call sites across 150+ modules** that the newer `register(FlagSpec)` signature silently broke (30 boot tracebacks were the visible subset). Hand-migrating was infeasible + anti-DRY; the root-cause fix is a **single backward-compatible adapter** at the one API boundary: `FlagRegistry.register()` now accepts the legacy kwargs and normalizes them into a `FlagSpec` via `_spec_from_legacy` (string→enum mapping for `type_`/`category`; bare posture strings dropped; unknown values degrade to safe defaults; never raises). One change fixed all callers + **eradicated every boot traceback (verified live: 30 → 0)**; canonical `register(FlagSpec)` unchanged. (2) **The Oracle 158 s freeze was NOT gather-able** — `_load_cache` is a single ~1.1 GB `pickle.loads`. The deferred-init path already existed but was *defeated* by the synchronous, **GIL-bound** deserialize blocking the loop. Slice 111 tried the operator-suggested `asyncio.to_thread` lift — and **empirically falsified it** (see §51.11.12). Also: infinite-soak config (`SHADOW_MAX_WALL_SECONDS=0` for the 12–18 mo deployment). 13 tests + 64 FlagRegistry regression green.

**§51.11.12 — Slice 112 (Process-Isolated Oracle — the GIL bypass).** **The honest negative result that defined the arc:** Slice 111's `to_thread` cache-load was *measured* in a live soak and **did nothing** — the boot log showed **55 lines, then 165 s of total silence, then resume**: the worker thread held the GIL for the entire 166 s `pickle.loads`, starving the asyncio loop *identically to an inline load*. `to_thread` cannot unblock a GIL-bound deserialize. This was reported as a failure, not papered over — and it precisely diagnosed the only real fix: **a separate process = a separate GIL.** Delivered `oracle_ipc.py`: the Oracle runs in its OWN OS process (own GIL) so the 1.1 GB load + the in-RAM `networkx` graph (which `shortest_path`/`simple_cycles` *require* — the reason a lazy-sqlite backend was rejected as mathematically impossible) never touch the engine loop. `AsyncOracleProxy` covers the audited **3-method** surface (`incremental_update` / `get_metrics` / `get_context_for_improvement`) over a spawn-context `Pipe`; resilience invariant: severed pipe → fail in-flight calls → narrate high-severity `OracleCrash` → bounded-backoff **respawn** → budget-exhaust to DEGRADED, **never crashing GLS**; structured `OracleNotReady` graceful degradation during hydration. Plus `prune_isolated_nodes()` graph hygiene (degree-0 nodes are pure serialization bloat — traversal results provably invariant). The reverted `to_thread` was removed ("we leave no useless code behind"). 11 tests (crash→respawn, degraded-not-crash, traversal-invariance). **Verify-first note: slice-32's `ProcessPoolExecutor` is a per-file AST-parse offload, NOT whole-Oracle hosting — so it was the wrong scaffolding to "leverage"; the proxy is new, composed from `OracleReadiness` + `daemon_narrator`.**

**§51.11.13 — Slice 113 (Unified Async Oracle Adapter — live wiring).** A single `await`-able interface over either backend, selected by `JARVIS_ORACLE_PROCESS_ISOLATION_ENABLED`. `InProcessOracleAdapter` is a **transparent drop-in** over `TheOracle` — `__getattr__` delegates every non-overridden method (`find_nodes_in_file`, `get_callers`, traversal) so existing consumers (e.g. `blast_radius_adapter`) keep working; only the 3 engine methods became async. `IsolatedOracleAdapter` wraps the proxy + normalizes `OracleNotReady` → safe degraded values. Verify-first confirmed **exactly 5 live call sites** (the `" 2.py"`/`" 3.py"` matches were stale backups); the orchestrator's SYNC `_build_dependency_summary` uses the adapter's `.raw` to avoid an async cascade. **First empirical proof of the GIL-bypass (live soak):** `process_isolation=1`; the 1.1 GB graph hydrated **in the subprocess (327 s, off the critical path)** while **GLS booted in 27 s** (vs ~166 s) logging "Oracle already injected (**?** nodes)" — the adapter's graceful degradation working. **The Oracle boot-freeze was eliminated.** 22 tests green. *Honest residual surfaced by the same soak:* the co-booted gateway still dipped (~57 s, timeouts) during **other** in-process C-ext boots (ChromaDB / `EmbeddingService` / consciousness) — not the Oracle. That residual set up Slice 114.

**§51.11.14 — Slice 114 (Gateway Decoupling — the invincible UI).** The co-boot topology was the root flaw: a UI sharing the engine's single event loop can never be 100 % responsive, because *any* GIL-heavy subsystem (vector loads, future ops) starves it. `telemetry_broker.py` severs the coupling: the gateway runs in its **OWN OS process** (`spawn_gateway_process`), and telemetry crosses on a bounded **`multiprocessing.Queue`** (stdlib, no external dep) — engine-side `publish_frame` is **non-blocking + drop-oldest** (the FSM never blocks on the UI), gateway-side `drain_queue_to_manager` reads off *its* own loop (engine freezes can't reach it). **Verify-first reframe: Phase 3 (deferring ChromaDB/embedding init) was deliberately NOT built** — once the gateway is decoupled it is immune to those freezes (they only affect the *engine's* own responsiveness, a separate concern), and they hold the GIL on C-ext init so threading wouldn't help (the §51.11.12 lesson). Building it would be redundant code chasing a solved problem. Master `JARVIS_GATEWAY_DECOUPLED_ENABLED` §33.1 default-FALSE. 7 tests (drop-oldest, drain fan-out + clean-stop, queue bridge). **THE INVINCIBILITY PROOF (live soak, `git switch main` → Slice 114, infinite wall):** the gateway spawned in its own process; **10 consecutive `:8000` health probes returned 200 with ZERO timeouts while the engine was pegged at 42–66 % CPU** booting its heavy subsystems — the *exact* window that timed out (000) under co-boot. **Head-to-head, the decoupled UI did not blink.** This is the arc's marquee receipt: not "merged," but *observed working* — the empirical-receipt discipline the §51.11.12 negative result demanded, applied to the positive result too.

> **Arc honesty ledger.** The 10/10 invincibility probe is ~40 s of early boot (the prior failure window) — strong but not the full 327 s hydration; complete confirmation is a sustained operator probe. Operational debt flagged, not hidden: an accumulated **~86 `aegis.daemon`/`async_pr_janitor` processes + 34 orphaned `multiprocessing.spawn` workers** from prior killed soaks were observed (the 34 orphans reaped during the Sovereign Ignition reset; the daemons left untouched, pending operator authorization). The repository was purged of all 7 merged feature branches (109–114 + revert), `main` re-synced local+remote, working tree switched to Slice-114 code, and the organism re-ignited on its decoupled runtime.

### §51.11.B — The Adversarial Proving Ground & Bounded Order-2 RSI Arc (Slices 115–119, 2026-06-06)

*The arc that turned the cage from an engineering assertion into a cryptographically-receipted proof, gave the immune system the ability to synthesize its own antibodies (operator-gated), proved the egress invariant by forgery, and — the capstone — wired Second-Order RSI (M10, the "Neurosurgeon") into the live orchestrator while keeping the §1 Zero-Order-Doll bound absolute. This is the dissertation's empirical spine: every safety claim in it is now a re-runnable receipt, and the standing research debt from §51.1 ("Iron Gate prevents deception / Anti-Venom contains RSI are engineering assertions, not theorems") is materially paid down — the assertions now carry deterministic, tamper-evident evidence. Verify-first overturned a literal premise in this arc too: Slice 118's "5 dormant modules to wire" were **hallucinated — none existed**; the egress lease + recursion gate were **already live** (Aegis + Slice 104), so the slice pivoted from "build a duplicate egress daemon" to "falsify the existing one." A catastrophic blind-wire of non-existent safety code into the live FSM was prevented by the audit.*

**§51.11.15 — Slice 115 (Blue/Red Adversarial Falsification Matrix).** The proving ground. **Red** composes the existing `adversarial_sweep` (corpus × 8 mutation operators × the cage — no duplicate FSM) + a NEW recursion-depth siege (drives `evaluate_recursion_gate` past `MAX_RECURSION_DEPTH`). **Blue** = `BlueEvidenceLedger`: an append-only, **hash-chained** `dissertation_evidence.jsonl` where each receipt carries `sha256(payload)` + verdict + a chain link (`record_hash = sha256(prev_hash ‖ canonical)`); `verify_ledger` detects any post-hoc tampering. `--siege-mode` runs it in the background during a soak. **Honest framing (load-bearing):** the ledger records the TRUE block/escape rate — it does NOT fabricate 100 % containment; known-gap escapes are logged *as escapes*. Live capstone soak result: **95.1 % variant-level block rate (39/41), recursion gate 2/2 halted, chain verified intact.** 7 tests.

**§51.11.16 — Slice 116 (Adaptive Immune Synthesis Engine — SAFE/bounded).** The safety reframe that defines the dissertation: "autonomously LLM-synthesize a cage rule and hot-load it" is an Order-2 RSI driver — refused. Built the bounded version: `antibody_synthesizer.py` does **deterministic** synthesis (analyze the escape's AST signature → a pure structural matcher; never LLM — the safety substrate must not be prompt-injectable, else "the adversary writes its own antibody"). Pipeline: **synthesize → validate (blocks-escape + ZERO clean-control FP + monotonic-tighten) → SHADOW proposal → operator-promote** (`promote_antibody` is fail-closed, refuses without explicit operator approval). Hot-swappable `AntibodyRegistry` loads *approved* antibodies live (no restart), consulted ADDITIVELY on top of the built-in SemanticGuardian patterns. 9 tests incl. the closed loop (escape → synth → operator-promote → hot-swap → same payload BLOCKED → clean controls still pass).

**§51.11.17 — Slice 117 (Synaptic Integration).** Closes the wiring gap: a verified siege ESCAPE → the exact escaping AST source is DETERMINISTICALLY re-derived from `(seed_name, strategy)` via `build_corpus` + `generate_mutations` (the sweep records metadata only — verify-first) → fed to the immune synthesizer → a SHADOW proposal. `GET /api/observability/antibody-proposals` exposes proposals + the "[IMMUNE SYSTEM ALERT] Awaiting Operator Approval" banner to the Command Center. **Capstone-run honest finding:** the live siege proposed ZERO antibodies — *correctly*, because the 2 escapes were quine/runtime-class, not the introspection-attribute class the deterministic synthesizer can fingerprint zero-FP. It DECLINED rather than fabricate. That honesty IS the theorem.

**§51.11.18 — Slice 118 (Aegis Egress-Invariant Falsification).** Verify-first killed the original premise (5 named "dormant" modules — `egress_broker`/`budget_authority`/`trust_tier`/`immutable_budget_state_machine`/`causal_lineage` — **all NOT FOUND**; egress already live via Aegis; recursion gate already wired). Pivoted to *proving* the real invariant: `aegis_lease_forgery.py` fires three forgery vectors at the **real** Aegis verifier (`validate_lease_token`) — **no-lease → `invalid_format`, forged-HMAC → `invalid_signature`, expired → `expired` (ALL rejected); valid control → `valid` (accepted — proves the verifier rejects forgeries *specifically*, not by blanket-denying)**. Each → a Blue receipt; `bridge_fails_closed()` pins that `acquire_call_lease` has no `except` in the lease path (no silent fallback). 9 deterministic tests. **The FSM cannot make an upstream API call without a valid Aegis lease — now cryptographically receipted.**

**§51.11.19 — Slice 119 (Bounded M10 Integration — the capstone).** M10 (the ArchitectureProposer / "Neurosurgeon" / Second-Order RSI) now has a **live-path reference in the orchestrator**, changing the §51-audit's "**0 orchestrator references**" finding — but bounded absolutely by the §1 Zero-Order-Doll invariant. `m10_synapse.py` (gated `JARVIS_M10_SYNAPSE_ENABLED`, §33.1 default-FALSE): `evaluate_m10_routing` triggers on high entropy / repeated failures and can ONLY return `forced_tier = APPROVAL_REQUIRED` (no self-authorizing route exists in the code); `propose_structural_upgrade` synthesizes → persists PENDING → **NEVER executes** (AST-pinned: the module imports nothing from `change_engine`/the apply path). The orchestrator hook (beside the existing "observe → APPROVAL_REQUIRED" force) routes M10 to the human gate; the Slice-104 recursion-depth gate bounds it independently. `GET /api/observability/m10-proposals` surfaces the AST diff for the operator's signature. 11 tests incl. the closed loop (high-entropy failure → propose → APPROVAL_REQUIRED → diff queued, NOT executed). **The Reverse Russian Doll is structurally complete: First-Order live; Second-Order wired-but-bounded; the operator the un-bypassable signature authority.**

**§51.11.20 — Slice 120 (The Sovereign Layer-4 Roadmap Authority — BOUNDED).** The bridge that lets the 12–18 month evidence clock (T5) run **unattended** without dissolving the Zero-Order Doll. `layer4_roadmap_authority.py` (gated `JARVIS_LAYER4_ROADMAP_ENABLED`, §33.1 default-FALSE) ingests an operator-signed `.jarvis/roadmap.signed.yaml`, **cryptographically verifies the operator's signature** (composes the *exact* Aegis HMAC-SHA256 token codec — `_encode_token`/`_decode_token`/`TokenVerdictKind` — no reinvented crypto), and for the **safe, explicitly-authorized scopes only** auto-resolves the approval prompt so Green ops run without a human in the loop for each one.

**The load-bearing refusal (§1).** The operator's brief said "fully suppress *all* APPROVAL_REQUIRED prompts." Taken literally that *removes the recursion bound* — a single signature (forged, or stale at month 12) could switch off the human gate on the very operations the cage exists to protect. We **refused the "all"** and built the bounded form: an **un-signable floor** that `may_suppress_approval` checks *before* the signature or scope is even read. **No signature can ever suppress approval for** SAFETY/BLOCKED-tier ops, Order-2/M10 cognitive self-modification, any op whose self-mod chain would exceed the Slice-104 recursion bound, or any governance/cage touch — those **always** escalate to a live operator decision. This is *delegated autonomy within a signed boundary*, never the removal of the boundary.

**Fail-closed + bounded budget.** Every defect — missing operator key, missing/garbled signature, bad HMAC, body-hash mismatch (tamper), expiry — returns a non-VALID authorization that collapses the system back to **per-PR human review** (the legacy safe default); the loader never raises. Budget/recursion bounds **only tighten**: a roadmap requesting depth 99 or $10,000 is clamped to the autonomous Slice-104 cap and the hard budget ceiling (the signature cannot *buy* more recursion or spend than the safety maxima allow). The orchestrator wiring is **escalation-only** (it can only re-assert `APPROVAL_REQUIRED`, never relax a tier — the auto-resolution UX lives in the harness), default-off → byte-identical, try/except-isolated so a malformed roadmap can never break the loop. `--layer4-autonomous` arms it on the soak. **21 tests** prove the fail-closed crypto (forged/tampered/expired/keyless → no autonomy), the un-signable floor (a VALID roadmap still cannot auto-approve an Order-2/M10 op, a recursion breach, a governance touch, or an APPROVAL_REQUIRED tier), and the budget clamps. **This is the T4 mechanism — built and proven; the operator's standing signature is the one thing that remains, by design.**

**§51.11.21 — Slice 121 (The Adversarial Volume & Concurrency-Hardening Matrix).** Authorized as "The Hyper-Accelerated Temporal Simulation Matrix"; **renamed for honesty after a verify-first reframe.** The directive was to "compress 12–18 months of wall-clock evidence into hours" by running 50+ concurrent loops. **The load-bearing correction: parallelism is not time-compression.** The T5 clock is a *duration / endurance* property (the cage holding across calendar time — dependency drift, slow state accumulation, naturally-arising operations); 50 instances × 1 hour is *throughput*, not 50 hours of soak, and nowhere near months of calendar exposure (the "9 women can't make a baby in 1 month" error). Stamping "≈N months simulated" into the dissertation ledger would be a **false attestation a committee would catch instantly**, discrediting the entire evidence corpus — so we refused it. The harness instead produces two *genuinely defensible* statistics that **complement, never substitute for**, the calendar soak: **adversarial volume/breadth** (escape rate over a large mutated sample) and **concurrency correctness** (the chain holds under load). `temporal_matrix.py` (gated `JARVIS_TEMPORAL_MATRIX_ENABLED`, §33.1 default-FALSE) composes Slice 115 (`BlueEvidenceLedger`/`verify_ledger`) + Slice 84 (`run_sweep`: corpus × mutation operators × the live cage) — no reinvented ledger/crypto/corpus.

Two further design corrections, also confident: **(1) read-only siege, not 50 live self-modifying organisms** — the matrix fans out the *cage evaluation* off-hot-path (the Slice 115 pattern), never 50 unsupervised `GovernedLoopService` mutators (50× blast radius + budget burn + git/worktree chaos for zero added evidence). **(2) A hash chain is irreducibly sequential** — a truly "lock-free append" to one linear chain is mathematically impossible (`record_hash = sha256(prev_hash ‖ record)` depends on its predecessor). The correct pattern: **parallelize the expensive, pure work (cage evaluation), serialize only the cheap chain-link.** `drive_concurrent_siege` runs N producer threads through ONE `threading.Lock`-guarded `ThreadSafeLedger` → one provably-unbroken chain; the production CLI parallelizes evaluation and lets the single main process link. The `MatrixReport` carries `evidence_kind="adversarial_volume_concurrency"` + a `disclaimer` and emits NO calendar-equivalence field. **7 tests** prove the marquee (1600 receipts across 16 concurrent threads → `verify_ledger` True, sequence numbers contiguous with no lost/duplicated writes) + the honesty invariant (schema forbids any "months/years simulated" key). Live-cage smoke: a real concurrent siege ran **570 attacks / 550 blocked / 3.51 % escape / chain intact** (matching the documented cage residual). `./scripts/launch_simulation_matrix.sh --concurrency 50` ignites it behind a prominent honesty banner. Slice 115 regression clean (8/8). **The bottleneck remains the T5 calendar clock — this slice strengthens the *robustness* axis, not the *duration* axis, and says so on every receipt.**

**§51.11.22 — Slice 122 (The Sovereign Cryptographic Key Manager & Dynamic Synthesis).** The Layer-4 ignition infrastructure: provisions the operator's signing authority with **zero hardcoding** — and, in doing so, fixes a genuine cryptographic weakness in Slice 120. **The root-cause upgrade: Slice 120 verified roadmaps with symmetric HMAC, but with HMAC whoever can *verify* can also *forge* — if the loop holds the key to check a roadmap, it can mint its own and self-authorize.** Slice 122 moves the Layer-4 signature to **asymmetric Ed25519** (`sovereign_keys.py`, gated `JARVIS_SOVEREIGN_KEYS_ENABLED`, §33.1 default-FALSE): the operator holds the **private** key, the loop is given **only the public key** (`.jarvis/layer4_operator.pub`). The loop can verify but **cannot forge — a mathematical guarantee, not a policy.** `verify_signed_roadmap` gained an additive ed25519 branch (routed before the HMAC fallback; the symmetric path stays byte-identical for backward-compat).

**Zero hardcoding, real air-gap.** The Ed25519 private key is **`scrypt(passphrase, salt)`** (stdlib `hashlib.scrypt`, no third-party KDF) — derived live from a passphrase the operator types, **never written to disk**. Only the salt + public key + a signature-verifier are persisted; the private key and passphrase never are (proven: a test asserts the passphrase bytes never appear in any on-disk file). The loop, run headless, has no passphrase → cannot derive the private key → cannot sign. **Single-user honesty:** on a single-user OS there is no kernel separation between "the AI" and "the operator" (same user), so the air-gap is *cryptographic + procedural* (the private key exists only transiently in an interactive operator session), backstopped by the un-signable floor (§1) which holds even if every key leaked.

**Dynamic synthesis (Phase 2):** `roadmap_synthesizer.py` audits recent commit scopes + tier state → drafts an **unsigned, authority-free** `.jarvis/roadmap.draft.yaml` with a conservative SAFE scope allow-list (docs/tests/observability — never governance/cage/Order-2, which are un-signable anyway), recursion clamped to the Slice-104 cap, a bounded ~12-month expiry. The draft grants nothing until signed.

**Phase 3 reframe — the refusal grounded in the codebase's own invariant.** The brief asked for a "one-click sign" button in the React Command Center on the FastAPI gateway. But `observability_gateway.py` *itself* declares (line 23): *"read-only over the web… a browser endpoint that flipped authority would be a sovereignty leak past the Zero-Order Doll."* A web sign-button is **exactly** that leak — a POST that mints unattended authority, reachable by any same-machine process (the loop included). So we exposed the **draft read-only** (`GET /api/observability/layer4-roadmap-draft` — draft + signing status, `signing_surface="local_cli_only"`, `armed=false`) and kept **signing as a deliberate local operator CLI act** (`python3 -m …sovereign_keys sign`, passphrase-gated). This is safer *and* consistent with the existing architecture; the full React tab is deferred (no React app exists in-repo, and a clickable web-sign is the wrong security boundary regardless). **10 tests** prove the full operator round-trip (provision → synthesize → sign → the loop verifies VALID with the public key only, and the un-signable floor still rejects an Order-2 op on that valid roadmap), the air-gap (a roadmap signed by a foreign key is rejected `INVALID_SIGNATURE`; wrong passphrase cannot load the private key; the passphrase is never on disk), and fail-closed (tampered body / no pubkey / expired → not VALID). Slice 120 regression clean (21/21). `cryptography` added to requirements. **T4 is now armable end-to-end: the operator provisions a key, reviews the draft, signs locally — and only then can the unattended T5 clock begin.**

**§51.11.23 — Slice 123 (Production Isolation & Hygiene Matrix).** Born from *live telemetry*: the first armed T5 launch verified Layer-4 flawlessly (`valid/ok(ed25519)`, floor holding) but exposed two production-readiness gaps — (a) the boot replayed **81 provenance-less recovery ops** from prior crashed sessions, all escalating to `manual_intervention_required` and starving fresh Layer-4-eligible work; (b) a **~2.5-min in-process Oracle load freeze** (`process_isolation=false`). Slice 123 closes both **architecturally, composing existing mechanism**.

**Phase 1 — Provenance Quarantine** (`boot_recovery_quarantine.py`, gated `JARVIS_BOOT_RECOVERY_QUARANTINE_ENABLED`, §33.1 default-FALSE): when a recovery op trips `boot_recovery_missing_provenance`, its raw payload is sequestered to `.jarvis/quarantine/{ts}_{op}.json` and marked `quarantined`, so it stops re-clogging the intake on every restart. **Additive** — the existing escalation/postmortem is untouched (auditability preserved); **best-effort** — wrapped so a quarantine write failure never breaks recovery (proven: unwritable dir → returns None, recovery continues); path-traversal-safe filenames; non-JSONable payloads degrade to repr. 7 tests.

**Phase 2 — Process-Isolated Oracle: VERIFY-FIRST found it ALREADY BUILT.** The directive said "rewrite the init sequence to spawn the graph load in a decoupled process" — but Slices 112/113 already shipped exactly that: `oracle_ipc.AsyncOracleProxy` (separate-GIL worker process) + `oracle_adapter.make_oracle_adapter()` which returns the `IsolatedOracleAdapter` when `JARVIS_ORACLE_PROCESS_ISOLATION_ENABLED` is set, and the harness already calls it. The boot froze only because that flag was unset. **So Slice 123 ENABLES the existing mechanism (no rewrite — that would be the duplication the mandate forbids)**; the 18 Slice-112/113 isolation tests confirm it's sound.

**Phase 3 — `--production-soak` profile** (in the harness arg layer, not buried in the script): one flag overrides the battle-test defaults to a real T5 run — `cost-cap=25.00`, `idle-timeout=0`, `max-wall-seconds=0` — and `setdefault`s the isolation + quarantine env flags. **Explicit `--cost-cap`/`--idle-timeout`/`--max-wall-seconds` still win** (detected via `sys.argv`, not the parsed value). Plus an operator-quality-of-life fix: `launch_shadow_soak.sh` now lets every Karen-voice flag respect an existing env value, so a run can be silenced with `JARVIS_KAREN_VOICE_ENABLED=0 ./scripts/launch_shadow_soak.sh …` (no code edit).

**Phase 4 — clean ignition (operator command):** `JARVIS_LAYER4_ROADMAP_ENABLED=1 JARVIS_SOVEREIGN_KEYS_ENABLED=1 JARVIS_KAREN_VOICE_ENABLED=0 ./scripts/launch_shadow_soak.sh --production-soak --layer4-autonomous`. 25 tests green (quarantine 7 + composed isolation 18); zero edits to the isolation mechanism itself. **The clock can now run clean: no cruft-clog, no GIL freeze, on the operator-signed roadmap.**

**§51.11.24 — Slice 124 (Autonomous Economic Failover Router).** The first clean production soak (Slice 123) ran for hours and surfaced the *real* blocker, by telemetry: **DoubleWord returned `http_402 "Account balance too low"`** — out of credits. BACKGROUND-routed OpportunityMiner ops (read-only scans) couldn't generate (BACKGROUND has no Claude fallback by policy), so $0 spent, no candidate, the Layer-4 gate never reached. Slice 124 makes provider economics self-healing.

**Phases 1+2 — `economic_router.py`** (gated `JARVIS_ECONOMIC_ROUTER_ENABLED`, §33.1 default-FALSE): a pure, bounded decision. On a HARD economic block (402 balance / 429 rate-limit), a **micro-op** (context under `JARVIS_ECONOMIC_MICRO_OP_TOKENS`, default 1500) cascades to the **cheapest Claude tier** to preserve momentum; a **massive-context op stays QUEUED** until the cheap provider returns. **Mutation safety preserved**: a mutating micro-op still needs the existing `JARVIS_BACKGROUND_ALLOW_FALLBACK` opt-in (only read-only micro-ops cascade autonomously). **No hardcoded model** (CLAUDE.md mandate): the cheap tier resolves from `JARVIS_ECONOMIC_FAILOVER_MODEL` (policy yaml has no cheap tier); empty → default fallback. Verify-first found the BACKGROUND→Claude cascade *already exists* (Defect #5 read-only reflex) — Slice 124 EXTENDS it with the economic size-gate + cheap-model selection, wired as a fail-open consult in the candidate_generator queue branch (default-off → byte-identical). 14 tests. **Honest scope:** the dedicated cheap-provider *instance* swap (vs. the default Sonnet fallback) is a documented follow-up — threading a per-call model override through the 100-line `_call_fallback` was judged too invasive to rush; the decision + size-gate + model-resolution + the unblock ship now.

**Phase 3 — starvation fix.** The confirmed `ControlPlaneStarvation lag_ms~3200` traced to `opportunity_miner_sensor.scan_once`: its `_is_production_code → continue` skip-path awaits nothing, spinning the loop between coarse `cooperative_yield_every_n` slots. A guaranteed `await asyncio.sleep(0)` per file iteration caps FSM lag (composes the existing Slice-12L offload hardening). **Phase 4** relaunch enables the router + a cheap failover model in env. The clock can now generate Layer-4 evidence **regardless of DW credit state**.

**§51.11.25 — Slice 125 (Aegis Credential Bootstrap + Health Probe — the real root cause).** Verify-first OVERTURNED my own Slice-124 premise. The operator asserted the DW key was funded; direct probes confirmed it: the `.env` key returned **HTTP 200 on every model** (incl. the exact `Qwen3.5-35B`/`397B`/`DeepSeek-V4-Flash` the soak `402`'d on). So the soak's `402 "balance too low"` was **never out-of-credits** — it was an **Aegis credential-injection gap**: the funded `.env` key wasn't in the process env when `aegis_preflight` snapshotted credentials for the daemon, so the daemon injected an empty token and DW billed the free ($0) tier. Slice 124's economic router was treating a *symptom*; this is the *cause*.

**Root invariant enforced:** `credential_env_loader.py` (stdlib-only, allowlist-only) loads the funded provider keys from `.env` into the env **immediately before the Aegis snapshot** (wired as step 0 of `aegis_preflight`, before the `creds = {...}` capture). Guarantees: **no `source .env`** (line-by-line `KEY=VALUE` parse — a hostile `.env` can't exec shell); **explicit exports win** (only fills empty names); **no secret ever logged** (redacted `sha256(value)[:8]` fingerprints only). A bash-native twin in `launch_shadow_soak.sh` (step 0) does the same before the first python subprocess. **Verified live:** the loader populates the real funded key (`sha256:6c4bf566`, len 46) into a fresh pre-snapshot env.

**Fail-loud health probe:** `credential_probe.py` runs two arms at boot (direct funded key vs Aegis-routed) and classifies — `direct 200 + aegis 402/401 → AEGIS_CREDENTIAL_INJECTION_FAILED` (NOT `provider_out_of_credits`); `direct 401/402 → OPERATOR_CREDENTIAL_PROBLEM`; network → `TRANSPORT_PROBLEM`. A fatal verdict **halts the boot** (`sys.exit(2)`) so a broken credential never silently `402`s for hours and burns Claude. Gated `JARVIS_AEGIS_CREDENTIAL_PROBE_ENABLED`; redacted logging. Composes the existing `aegis_provider_bridge` (`dw_aegis_base_url` / `dw_session_auth_header`) — no duplicate credential registry, no hardcoded keys. **13 tests** (`.env`-fills-absent-key, explicit-export-wins, malformed/missing-`.env`-clean-no-leak, 402→injection-failure-not-out-of-credits, redaction). This closes the blocker that defeated four soaks.

**§51.11.26 — Slice 126.5 (Cryptographic State Telemetry — the ghost exposed & killed).** The blocker that defeated FIVE soaks, finally resolved by making the runtime credential observable. After exhaustively proving the Aegis injection code was *statically correct* (loader→snapshot→spawn→inject all sound; funded key flows through every step), the only remaining explanation was a runtime value invisible to static analysis. Slice 126.5 added **permanent redacted fingerprint telemetry** (`sha256[:8]`, never the raw key) at the two exact points: the daemon's **env-load** (`daemon.py build_app`) and the **injection microsecond** (`forwarding.py`). One live run exposed the ghost: daemon env-load `DOUBLEWORD_API_KEY = sha256:f4354214`, injection = same `f4354214` — **no load→inject mutation** (injection always faithful), but **the daemon loaded the WRONG key** (the funded key is `sha256:6c4bf566`). Root cause: a **stale, unfunded `DOUBLEWORD_API_KEY` in `backend/.env`** (`f4354214`) auto-loaded ahead of the funded repo-root `.env` (`6c4bf566`) and preserved by Slice-125's explicit-env-wins. **Surgical eradication:** neutralized the stale `backend/.env` line (gitignored/local; value never read or printed). **Permanent guard:** the credential loader now emits a loud redacted CONFLICT warning whenever an existing env credential differs from the operator's `.env` — so a sibling-`.env` shadow can never hide again. **Kill-shot verified live:** post-fix the daemon env-load + injection both show the funded `sha256:6c4bf566`, **402-count = 0**, and a **DoubleWord completion succeeded**. The DW pipeline is online. 15 tests. (Telemetry was the only way to repair a statically-correct bridge — verify-first illumination, not a guessed mutation.)

### §51.11.D — Slice 127 BLUEPRINT (DEFERRED — Multi-Lane Self-Healing Circuit Breaker)

**Status: NOT YET BUILT.** Architecture locked here for the next session (deferred off a depleted context budget — a sloppy rewrite of the generation gatekeeper is unacceptable). This is a specification, not a changelog entry.

**Problem (verify-first localized, 2026-06-06):** A single `401` on the **`/v1/models` health-probe** (an Aegis *passthrough*, not a generation call) is classified `TERMINAL_CONFIG` (`provider_retry_classifier.py:169` — `_HTTP_STATUS_TERMINAL_CONFIG = {401,403,404}`) and trips the **GLOBAL** breaker to sticky `OPEN_TERMINAL` (`circuit_breaker.py:54-55`). Once global-terminal, **every** subsequent op short-circuits in ~9ms (`all_providers_exhausted:circuit_breaker_tripped:terminal_config`), bricking the entire organism — including the now-working DoubleWord chat-completions lane. Observed live in session `bt-2026-06-07-040933`: `401-count=1` → `terminal_config trips=16`, zero DW completions, requiring a manual restart. A Tier-D organism must self-heal, not brick.

**What ALREADY exists (compose, do NOT rebuild):** `circuit_breaker.py` already implements the full self-healing FSM — `CircuitState = {CLOSED, OPEN_TRANSIENT (backoff-then-probe), HALF_OPEN (probing recovery), OPEN_TERMINAL (sticky)}`, full-jitter exponential backoff, and `record_success() in HALF_OPEN → CLOSED`. The recovery machinery is built; it just isn't reachable for these failures because (a) the scope is global and (b) terminal is sticky.

**Core directives (the three changes):**
1. **`CircuitScope` → `PER_PROVIDER`.** Today `CircuitScope = {PER_OP, GLOBAL}` (`circuit_breaker.py:175`). Add `PER_PROVIDER` and key the breaker registry by provider lane (`doubleword` / `anthropic` / `prime`). A trip in the Anthropic lane MUST NOT touch the DoubleWord lane. Keep `GLOBAL` only for genuinely cross-cutting structural failures (e.g. `TERMINAL_STRUCTURAL` from a sovereignty breach), never for a single provider's config/quota hit.
2. **Quarantine health-probe failures from the generation breaker.** A `401`/`403`/`404` on a non-generation **passthrough** endpoint (`/v1/models`, `/v1/files`, `/v1/batches*` — `EndpointKind.PASSTHROUGH`, daemon.py:202) MUST be mathematically prevented from escalating the **generation** (`EndpointKind.LLM_COMPLETION`) breaker to `OPEN_TERMINAL`. Health-probe auth failures are informational, not generation-fatal. Tag probe-origin failures (extend `CircuitTripOrigin`) and exclude them from the LLM_COMPLETION lane's terminal accounting.
3. **Wire the existing `OPEN_TRANSIENT → HALF_OPEN → CLOSED` backoff into the per-lane routing matrix.** When a provider lane trips, pause ONLY that lane for the calculated full-jitter backoff, then auto-probe (canary) and reset to `CLOSED` on success — no process restart. Transient signatures (0-token empty response, 5xx) must route to `OPEN_TRANSIENT` (recoverable), never `OPEN_TERMINAL`. Add an explicit `EMPTY_RESPONSE` → `RETRY_TRANSIENT` mapping in `provider_retry_classifier.py` `_FAILURE_MODE_DEFAULT` (alongside `SERVER_ERROR`/`TIMEOUT`) AND a producer-side `ProviderEmptyResponse` high-severity (non-fatal) signal where the 0-token/`first_token_ms=-1` response is detected (providers.py / candidate_generator.py generation path).

**Exact files + anchors:**
- `backend/core/ouroboros/governance/circuit_breaker.py` — `CircuitScope` (L175), `CircuitState` FSM (L165-172), terminal-trip table (L54-59), `record_failure`/`decision` consumer (L799-818). The breaker registry/lookup is where `PER_PROVIDER` keying goes.
- `backend/core/ouroboros/governance/provider_retry_classifier.py` — `_HTTP_STATUS_TERMINAL_CONFIG` (L169), `_FAILURE_MODE_DEFAULT` (L203), `classify()` (L219). Add `EMPTY_RESPONSE`→`RETRY_TRANSIENT`; add a probe-origin guard so health-probe 401s don't reach the generation lane as terminal.
- `backend/core/ouroboros/aegis/daemon.py` — `_make_passthrough_handler` (L228) vs `_make_llm_handler` (L190). Passthrough = health-probe class; tag its failures distinctly.
- Producer of the 0-token signal: the generation path emitting `provider= tokens=0 first_token_ms=-1 total_ms=9` (StreamRenderer/candidate_generator) — wire the `ProviderEmptyResponse` interceptor there.

**Invariants (non-negotiable):** PER_PROVIDER isolation is structural (Anthropic trip ⇏ DoubleWord trip); health-probe failures never brick generation; transient failures always recover via the existing HALF_OPEN path; `TERMINAL_STRUCTURAL` (sovereignty/§1) stays sticky-global by design. Tests-first: a per-lane isolation test (trip Anthropic, assert DW still CLOSED), a health-probe-quarantine test (401 on /v1/models ⇏ generation OPEN_TERMINAL), a recovery test (OPEN_TRANSIENT → backoff → HALF_OPEN canary → CLOSED with no restart), and the breaker regression suite must stay green.

**Verification gate:** after the fix, a fresh production soak must survive an injected health-probe 401 AND reach a real `LAYER4:` runtime line (the milestone unachieved across 6 soaks — now blocked only by this breaker + the natural arrival of a sensor-driven op). The DW credential path is already proven (Slice 126.5: 402=0, completion succeeded).

### §51.11.27 — Slice 127 BUILT (Economic Sovereign Matrix) — the verify-first correction of §51.11.D

**Status: P1 + P2 + P3 + P2.1 BUILT, tested, committed. The first bounded ignition soak (bt-2026-06-07) PROVED P1+P2 live (0 `terminal_config` bricks; Claude credit-400 → recoverable `terminal_quota`; `ECONOMIC TRIP` isolated the Claude lane + self-heals) and surfaced P2.1. Only P4 (a re-run soak on a lane that actually completes) remains.**

**P2.1 — fallback-skip gate (IMMEDIATE → DW failover).** The live soak exposed a routing blind spot: `_generate_immediate` does "Claude direct, skip DW", and the existing `should_allow_request` gate only covers Claude-as-*primary* — so IMMEDIATE ops kept grinding against the depleted Claude lane (`terminal_quota` ×N, no completion) instead of failing over to the funded DW lane. Fix: the Claude-direct path now consults the Claude lane breaker via a pure decision helper (`immediate_reroute_to_dw`); when the breaker is OPEN (economic/transport) it reroutes the op to the DW primary (`_call_primary`), while a HALF_OPEN probe still keeps Claude-direct so the lane self-heals. Master `JARVIS_FALLBACK_SKIP_GATE_ENABLED` (default-FALSE §33.1). 8 tests + wiring pin; 170 green.

**The blueprint was misdiagnosed (verify-first, ground truth from `bt-2026-06-07-040933` `debug.log`).** §51.11.D claimed a `/v1/models` **401** health-probe trips a **GLOBAL** breaker sticky `OPEN_TERMINAL`, bricking all lanes. The canonical log (line 1592) proves otherwise:

```
fallback_err_class=BadRequestError
fallback_err_msg=Error code: 400 - 'Your credit balance is too low to access the Anthropic API...'
slice7e_decision=terminal_config
```

- The 16 trips were caused by **Claude HTTP 400 "credit balance too low"** — class `BadRequestError`, which is in `_TERMINAL_CONFIG_CLASSES` → `TERMINAL_CONFIG` → the **per-op** Slice-7 breaker sticky `OPEN_TERMINAL` on the 1st hit (`escalated_to_global=False`, 16 separate ops). **Not** a global breaker, **not** the 401.
- The `/v1/models` **401** is a benign `SemanticTriage` warning (line 46) that never reaches the generation breaker. §51.11.D directive #2 (quarantine the 401) addressed a **non-problem** and was **descoped**.
- Root cause: a "credit balance too low" 400 is an **economic** refusal (recoverable once funded — the Anthropic twin of the DW 402 that Slice 124 already handles), misclassified as a **permanent config** fault.

**What was built (compose-first — operator's leverage-existing/avoid-duplication mandate):**

- **P1 — Economic reclassification (the real root fix).** `provider_retry_classifier.classify()` gains `failure_message` + `economic_reclassify` params; when an economic block is recognised (composing the canonical `economic_router.is_hard_economic_block`), it returns the recoverable `TERMINAL_QUOTA` instead of sticky `TERMINAL_CONFIG` — **no new RetryDecision member** (closed 4-value AST pin intact). The classifier stays **PURE-DATA** (AST-pinned: no `os.environ`); the env gate `JARVIS_ECONOMIC_RECLASSIFY_ENABLED` (default-FALSE §33.1) lives in `economic_router.economic_reclassify_enabled()`. The detector was **strengthened** to match Anthropic's actual "credit balance **is** too low" phrasing — the original "balance too low" marker missed it, and that miss **was** the bug. Wired at `candidate_generator` breaker call site (`str(inner_exc)` + gate). End-to-end cages prove: gate-on → recoverable `RETRY_AFTER_BACKOFF` (1st hit, breaker non-terminal); gate-off → byte-identical legacy brick.
- **P2 — Per-provider economic self-healing breaker.** The **existing** `ClaudeCircuitBreaker` is already a per-Anthropic-lane self-healing breaker (CLOSED/OPEN/HALF_OPEN + recovery window) — it just never tripped on economics. Composed via `record_economic_exhaustion()` (distinct counter; trips OPEN at a low threshold; self-heals via the existing recovery-window → HALF_OPEN → `record_success`). Master `JARVIS_CLAUDE_ECONOMIC_BREAKER_ENABLED` (default-FALSE). Wired at the fallback site so **future** ops route around the broke Claude lane (existing `should_allow_request` gate) and the lane recovers when funded — no session brick. **Per-provider isolation is realized by composing this existing per-lane breaker, NOT a parallel `CircuitScope.PER_PROVIDER` registry** (which would duplicate the lane-health mechanism — the operator's explicit anti-duplication mandate, endorsed when the misdiagnosis was surfaced).

- **P3 — DW transport dynamic exponential self-healing.** **Verify-first narrowed P3 to one change:** the DW lane recovery already self-heals (a `TRANSPORT_DEGRADED` verdict auto-probes back once stale via `dw_transport_degraded_preflight`) and `EMPTY_RESPONSE` is already recoverable (0-token → `DoublewordInfraError(status 0)` → `TIMEOUT`/`CONTENT_FAILURE` → `RETRY_TRANSIENT`) — so neither needed building. The only gap was the **hardcoded-default 120s STATIC** freshness window. New `dw_transport_recovery.py` (thread-safe singleton, **composes** `circuit_breaker.full_jitter_delay` — no new backoff math) replaces it with a **dynamic full-jitter exponential** window keyed to consecutive rupture *episodes*: `note_degraded()` (debounced by `base` → burst = 1 episode), `note_recovered()` (DW success → reset to 0 instantly), `dynamic_recovery_window_s()` = `max(base, full_jitter_delay(episode-1, base, cap))` (episode 1 = `base`; episode N up to `base·2^(N-1)`, capped). Master `JARVIS_DW_DYNAMIC_RECOVERY_ENABLED` (default-FALSE §33.1; knobs `JARVIS_DW_RECOVERY_BASE_S`=30, `JARVIS_DW_RECOVERY_CAP_S`=600). 3 gated, best-effort integration sites in `candidate_generator` (`_note_dw_candidate_success`→reset, `_note_dw_live_transport_degraded`→episode, `dw_transport_degraded_preflight`→dynamic window). 12 module tests + wiring pins; 137 green across the suite. **No byte-stream resume is claimed** — LLM completion streams cannot be byte-resumed mid-chunk; "recovery" is lane-level probe timing only (claiming otherwise would be a false attestation).

**Honest remaining scope.** P4 (the ignition soak — needs an operator-funded lane + ~40 min wall-clock to reach `LAYER4:`) is the only remaining piece. All P1–P3 masters default-FALSE; OFF is byte-identical to pre-127.

### §51.11.28 — Slice 128 BUILT (Oracle IPC daemonic-fix + Z3 SMT prover substrate)

Born from the Slice 127 soak telemetry (2026-06-07): the bounded soak proved the economic matrix end-to-end but could not COMPLETE an op when run **nested under the agent process tree** — the event loop starved (Oracle isolation-ON → daemonic-pool storm; isolation-OFF → in-process GIL load). Slice 128 makes the heavy-compute decoupling **structurally correct** (no "run it in a separate terminal" workaround) and lays the formal-proof foundation.

**P1 — In-process AST analyze for the isolated Oracle (kills the daemonic starvation).** **Verify-first: the robust IPC layer already exists** — `oracle_ipc.py` (Slice 112) is spawn-context **Pipe** IPC with crash-respawn, not naive multiprocessing. The crash was a precise defect: the Oracle worker is spawned **`daemon=True`** (`oracle_ipc.py:186`), and a daemonic process cannot have children — so the Oracle's inner `ast_compile_helper` `ProcessPoolExecutor` (via `oracle._index_file`) crashed `daemonic processes are not allowed to have children` (×4789 in the soak), churning the loop into 8–13 s starvation. Fix (compose, no rebuild): the Oracle is **already** off the main loop in its own subprocess, so the nested pool is redundant. `ast_compile_helper` gains a gated in-process analyze mode (`ast_helper_inprocess_enabled`, `JARVIS_AST_HELPER_INPROCESS_ENABLED`, default-FALSE) — when on, `_process_pool_analyze_for_oracle` dispatches the worker via `asyncio.to_thread` instead of the spawn pool (no nested children, no daemonic crash, the subprocess IPC loop stays responsive). `oracle_ipc._oracle_worker_main` enables it (`setdefault`) before `TheOracle` builds. Default-FALSE → the main process keeps the spawn pool byte-identical. 5 tests; `oracle_ipc` (7) + `ast_compile_helper` (23) regression green.

**P2 — SMT/Z3 invariant prover substrate (Phase 0).** Turns an engineering assertion into a **machine-checked theorem with a tamper-evident certificate** — **additive**, never replacing the deterministic `ShippedCodeInvariant` AST checks. `smt_invariant_prover.py`: `SmtSpec` (schema `smt.1`; `smt2` asserts the **negation** → PROVED iff Z3 `unsat`; optional `linked_invariant_name` composes `ShippedCodeInvariant`); `ProofVerdict` closed 5-value taxonomy; `prove()` runs Z3 **out-of-process** (`z3` CLI `-in`, hard timeout — a hang/crash can't wedge the engine) with an **injectable** solver runner so the verdict logic is unit-testable with no z3 installed; **import-guarded** (NEVER `import z3` at module top — AST-pinned; availability probed lazily); **default-FALSE** master `JARVIS_SMT_PROVER_ENABLED` → `UNAVAILABLE`; **fail-closed** (`is_proof_trustworthy` True ONLY for PROVED — UNKNOWN/timeout/UNAVAILABLE/ERROR/REFUTED can never yield a false proof); `attest_invariant()` appends a hash-chained receipt to `BlueEvidenceLedger` (the cryptographic certificate; `blocked=True` only for trustworthy PROVED). 15 tests, all green **without z3 installed**. Phase 0 ships the substrate, NOT a catalogue of proven theorems — proving the actual dissertation invariants ("Anti-Venom contains RSI") is the follow-on, and requires `z3-solver` provisioned.

**Honesty.** P1 is structurally proven by unit tests; the *full* starvation-free confirmation still wants a dedicated-terminal soak (the nested-agent CPU contention is environmental). P2 ships only the prover engine — no invariant is yet machine-proven (z3 absent here). All masters default-FALSE; OFF byte-identical.

### §51.11.29 — Slice 129 BUILT (Z3 provisioned + the FIRST machine-checked safety theorem)

The Slice 128 substrate goes live. **z3-solver 4.16 provisioned** (pinned in `requirements.txt`; still import-guarded + fail-closed when absent). The first JARVIS safety rule is translated into formal mathematics and **machine-proven with a cryptographic certificate**.

**The theorem (RRD Recursion-Depth Bound, `smt_encodings.recursion_bound_spec`).** The decision rule mirrored from `evaluate_recursion_gate` — `effective = chain_depth + 1`; `HALT iff effective > mx`; `mx = max_recursion_depth()` clamped `[1,16]` — is encoded as an SMT-LIB2 **inductive-safety** theorem: for ANY ceiling in the clamp range, an ALLOWED governance op can never push the applied chain depth past `mx` (the bound is un-escapable). PROVED iff Z3 returns `unsat` on the negation `∃ depth,mx: 0≤depth≤mx ∧ depth+1≤mx ∧ depth+1>mx`. **Live result (z3 4.16): `PROVED`**, certificate `c56da983…`, written to the hash-chained `BlueEvidenceLedger` (`dissertation_evidence.jsonl`, `attack_class=smt_invariant_proof`, `verdict=proved`, `blocked_by=z3:recursion_depth_gate`, `record_hash=375a53b8…`).

**Integrity controls.** (1) A **negative control** — an off-by-one *loosened* encoding — is correctly **REFUTED** (`sat`), proving the prover discriminates and the PROVED is not vacuous. (2) The encoding's **parameters** (clamp bounds, live ceiling) are extracted from the gate module; its decision **structure** (offset `+1`, comparator `>`) is mirrored from the code and anchored by a bytes-pin test (`test_gate_structure_pin`) so code drift forces re-derivation.

**Honest scope (the faithfulness gap).** This is a machine-checked proof that the recursion-gate's decision *logic, as encoded*, soundly enforces the ceiling — tied to the live parameters + structure-pinned. It does **NOT** yet prove the Python bytecode matches the encoding (verified-AST-extraction is future work) and is **ADDITIVE** — the deterministic `recursion_depth_gate` runtime check stays authoritative. It is the **first** theorem of the dissertation, not the full "Anti-Venom contains RSI" — that is a multi-theorem program this substrate now makes tractable. 5 tests (encoding + structure-pin + live PROVED + negative-control REFUTED + cert-in-ledger).

### §51.11.30 — Slice 130 BUILT (deterministic AST→SMT extraction — the faithfulness gap closed)

Slice 129's honest caveat ("proves the *encoded abstraction*, not the live bytecode") is now structurally closed. The SMT is no longer hand-mirrored — it is **extracted from the live `recursion_depth_gate.py` AST and compiled to Z3 dynamically**.

**`ast_to_smt_extractor.py`.** `extract_recursion_gate_logic(source)` deterministically walks `evaluate_recursion_gate` and extracts the decision pattern `effective = chain + <int>` / `if effective <cmp> mx[ + <int>]: HALT` into `(lhs_offset, comparator, rhs_offset)` plus the module clamp constants. `compile_recursion_bound_smt(logic)` compiles the **extracted** predicate into the inductive-safety negation (`allow ∧ effective>mx`; unsat=PROVED) — the offset and comparator come from the AST, nothing is hardcoded. `smt_encodings.recursion_bound_spec()` now **delegates** to the extractor (the canonical theorem is AST-derived). **FAIL-CLOSED:** any source the extractor doesn't recognize yields a non-provable spec — an unexpected shape can never produce a false certificate.

**The closed loop (live, z3 4.16).** Live source → **PROVED** (cert `8834560e…`, written to `dissertation_evidence.jsonl`, hash-chained). A developer **loosening** the bound (`if effective > mx + 1`) is auto-caught — the extractor re-derives a different formula and Z3 returns **REFUTED**. A **stricter** change (`>= mx`) still **PROVED**. An offset change (`+1 → +2`) produces a different formula. This is the operator's requirement: *alter the Python → the extractor catches the mutation → re-compiles the Z3 math → forces a new proof.*

**Honest scope.** This is a deterministic extractor for the recursion-gate decision **pattern**, fail-closed on anything else — NOT a general Python→SMT compiler (undecidable in general). It closes the faithfulness gap **for this invariant**: the proof now tracks the live AST, not a human abstraction. Generalizing the extractor to additional rules (the Governance Boundary Gate, the un-signable Layer-4 floor) is the follow-on toward the full containment theorem. 8 tests (extraction + compile + fail-closed + live PROVED + loosened-REFUTED + stricter-PROVED + offset-drift); prover suite (27) green.

### §51.11.31 — Slice 131 (The Cost Sovereign Matrix) — Phase 1 BUILT; Phase 2a + Phase 4 BLUEPRINT *(2026-06-07 — operator-driven: "are we optimizing token usage for O+V (Claude + DW)? ... I'm burning Claude API money but DW always has problems ... there has to be dead code not being used that we can use ... O+V needs to know what provider/LLM to use via Contextual Awareness Intelligence (CAI), like Cursor's auto ... SUPER DUPER BEEF IT UP")*

A verify-first cost/token audit + 2026 LLM-cost research (FrugalGPT/RouteLLM cascade, GPTCache semantic caching, prompt caching, Batch API 50%, context compaction → **70–85% stacked**). Confirmed the operator's hypothesis: high-ROI cost machinery was **built but switched OFF**.

**PHASE 1 — BUILT & MERGED (PR #69340, main `640ad5bac5`).** The immediate, verified money-saver, now live default-on:
- **Provider Response Cache** graduated to default-TRUE (`provider_response_cache.py` — exact-match, repo-state-keyed; **correctness-fail-closed**: any git diff re-keys, so a stale repo can never serve a wrong response; availability-fail-open → default-on only eliminates redundant identical-context calls).
- **Economic Router** graduated to default-TRUE (`economic_router.py` — only acts on the provider-FAILURE path DW 402/429, so default-on cannot raise happy-path spend).
- **No-hardcode refactor** (CLAUDE.md mandate): `economic_failover_model()` resolves the cheap Claude tier from `brain_selection_policy.yaml` → new `cost_optimization.claude_low_cost_model: claude-haiku-4-5` (`claude-3-5-haiku` is **retired**), `JARVIS_ECONOMIC_FAILOVER_MODEL` env override wins, zero `claude-*` string in code (test-pinned). 36 tests green. **Already LIVE (pre-existing, verified):** Claude prompt caching (system block, default-TRUE), SemanticTriage (cheap-35B NO_OP filter), context_compaction, cost_governor.

**PHASE 2a BLUEPRINT — tool-catalog cache restructuring (DEFERRED — invasive hot-path, do NOT rush).** Verify-first overturned the original premise: O+V's Venom tools are NOT a native Anthropic `tools=[]` array — they are **text** built by `_build_tool_section()` (`providers.py:1713`, called 2332/3131) and appended to the **volatile per-op lean prompt** (`parts.append(...)`, after preloaded files + task), so the stable tool catalog is **re-billed every op** (a genuine leak). `_CODEGEN_SYSTEM_PROMPT` (`providers.py:166`, the whole-file codegen instruction prompt, NOT the tool catalog) is a stable constant already cached via `_build_cached_system_blocks` (6086). **Root-cause fix (future):** restructure the lean-prompt assembly so stable content (tool catalog + schema rules + manifesto) sits in a cached PREFIX with its own `cache_control` breakpoint (≤4 cap; prefix order system→messages) and volatile content (task, source snapshot, preloaded files) follows AFTER — verified against `get_cache_stats` cache-hit telemetry. NOT a one-line add; requires careful hot-path surgery on a fresh budget.

**PHASE 2b / Phase 3 (DEFERRED).** P2b: Claude Batch API for BACKGROUND/SPECULATIVE → `/v1/messages/batches` (flat 50%; verified ZERO batch usage today; master `JARVIS_BATCH_ROUTING_ENABLED` default-FALSE; compose `should_skip_venom_for_route`). P3: semantic response cache — new module composing the existing `SemanticIndex`/bge-small (embed query intent → cosine-scan recent high-confidence cache → intercept near-match above threshold → $0; master `JARVIS_SEMANTIC_CACHE_ENABLED` default-FALSE; most self-contained of the remaining).

**PHASE 4 BLUEPRINT — THE CAI AUTONOMOUS ROUTER (the headline; AUTHORIZED for the next session).** The "Cursor-auto for O+V": autonomously pick the cheapest *capable* provider/model per op via Contextual Awareness Intelligence, escalating to heavyweights only when CAI signals high difficulty / low confidence. **COMPOSE the existing substrate (verified to exist — do NOT rebuild):**
- `backend/intelligence/context_awareness_intelligence.py` — `ContextAwarenessIntelligence.predict_intent(text)` / `analyze_context(data)` / `understand_with_reasoning(...)` → the pre-flight **complexity/intent classifier**.
- `backend/intelligence/model_selector.py` — `IntelligentModelSelector.select_best_model(QueryContext)` / `select_with_fallback(...)` (singleton `get_model_selector()`) → the **cost-aware model picker** (`QueryContext`, `ModelOption`).
- `backend/core/ouroboros/governance/route_decision_service.py` — `RouteDecisionService.decide(...)` / `select(...)` / `record_cost(...)` → the governance **route/provider decision + spend ledger**.
- `economic_router.py` (Phase 1) → the **failover matrix** when the chosen cheap tier 402/429s.

**Wiring (FrugalGPT cascade):** CAI `predict_intent`/`analyze_context` → difficulty+confidence signal → `IntelligentModelSelector.select_best_model(QueryContext{difficulty, urgency, route})` → dispatch to **cheapest capable tier first** (DoubleWord / Haiku for low-complexity) → **escalate** to heavyweights (Sonnet/Opus) ONLY when CAI signals high-difficulty OR low-confidence below an adaptive threshold → on cheap-tier 402/429, hand off to the EconomicRouter failover. Fuse the decision into `RouteDecisionService` (the existing governance seam — note `UrgencyRouter` routes by *urgency* today, NOT *difficulty*; Phase 4 adds the contextual/difficulty dimension). Master `JARVIS_CAI_ROUTER_ENABLED` default-FALSE; fully async, dynamic, adaptive; applies to DW + all providers; record_cost feeds the adaptive threshold (self-tuning). No hardcoded models — all tiers resolve from `brain_selection_policy.yaml`.
