Composite toward the North Star still ≈ 35%; the remaining 65% is runtime, vendor-stress reliability, and inward-RSI safety, not slices.


### §51.11.33 — The Soak Provider-Funding & Cost Structure *(2026-06-11 — operator-driven: "how much money do we need for the Claude provider to run a full soak cycle?")*

**LIVE DIAGNOSIS (bt-2026-06-12, dual-engine soak):** the soak was crash/exit-looping (~20 restarts/5h) with the autonomy chain stalled at dispatch. Root cause was NOT the code — it was **provider fuel**:

- **Claude = 402 (out of credits).** `[ClaudeCircuitBreaker] ECONOMIC TRIP (CLOSED -> OPEN) after 1 economic exhaustion (claude_lane_economic:402)` — the Anthropic account balance is empty, so the economic circuit breaker trips the Claude lane OPEN for 900s. **This is the tier to fund.**
- **DW = TIMEOUT (not 402).** `primary_name=doubleword-397b fsm_failure_mode=TIMEOUT` — DW's key is set/funded; it fails on the chronic vendor instability (oversubscribed GPU backend), which funding cannot fix.
- The lethal combination: DW primary times out -> cascades to Claude rescue -> Claude 402s -> both tiers down -> `circuit_breaker_tripped:terminal_quota` (53 trips) -> no generation completes -> session exits young -> restart:always churns. The §51.11.26 lesson recurred: **verify the credential/credit reality before code archaeology.**

**HONEST CAVEAT:** no MEASURED per-op cost exists yet — the soak has never completed a full op (always died on the 402s). The figures below are token-math estimates against published rates (Claude Sonnet-class ~$3/$15 per M in/out; cheapest tier `claude-haiku-4-5` $1/$5; DW ~$0.10/$0.40), to be replaced with measured data once a cycle completes.

**Per-op estimate (Venom agentic loop, ~8-15 LLM calls w/ S131 prompt-caching):** moderate op $0.20-1.00 on Sonnet; heavy multi-file COMPLEX + L2 repair $1-3; ~3x cheaper if economic-routed to Haiku.

**THE BIGGEST COST LEVER IS NOT CLAUDE — IT IS FUNDING DW TOO.** The Slice-215 positioning keeps Claude as per-round RESCUE while DW does cheap volume. If DW is dead/unfunded, the cascade rescues EVERY round on Claude (5-10x more expensive). Cheapest healthy soak = BOTH funded: DW absorbs volume at $0.002/op, Claude fires only on the failure tail + critical path.

**FUNDING GOALS (operator-facing, with the $10/session cost-cap as the per-session safety bound):**

| Goal | Both funded (intended) | Claude-only (DW dead) | What it proves |
|------|------------------------|------------------------|----------------|
| **G1 — Prove ONE autonomous op -> first PR** (the milestone) | $1-5 | $10-15 | The autonomy chain completes end-to-end once; first substantive autonomous code in the review queue |
| **G2 — Complete GOAL-001** (both sub-goals -> PR) | $3-15 | $20-40 | The roadmap-goal -> decomposition -> multi-step -> dispatch -> PR loop closes on a real goal |
| **G3 — Multi-day continuous soak** (ambient sensors + roadmap, several PRs, real autonomy) | $25-100/day | $100-300/day | Sustained proactive self-development + the §41.6 unsupervised-days evidence the grade depends on |

**OPERATOR RECOMMENDATION:** ~$20 Claude credits + top up nothing-needed-on-DW-balance (DW is timeout-limited not credit-limited) to prove G1 safely (bounded by the $10/session cap). $50-100 Claude for a real multi-day G3 soak. Cost guardrails already active: S131 response cache (dedupes repeat Claude calls), `JARVIS_THINKING_BUDGET_IMMEDIATE=0`, BG/SPEC pinned DW-only by topology, COST_CAP_90 Discord sentinel (alerts before the cap). **Two non-code prerequisites remain between "loop wired" and "loop runs": funded Claude credits + a host that does not sleep** (the soak Mac suspended overnight; Chronos honestly refused to count the slept hours).


### §51.11.34 — The Soak Reliability + Token-Economic Arc (Slices 217–224, 2026-06-12) *(operator-driven: "is O+V doing its job?" → "i'm burning Claude money fast" → "deep research on cost optimization")*

**The arc that turned the funded-but-idle organism into a measured, cost-armed, debugged system — and surfaced the honest truth that the autonomy blocker is NOT cost.** Eight slices, each a verify-first catch that overturned its own authorizing plan. Per-slice provenance in `memory/` (S217–S224).

**THE FIVE-LAYER ONION (each fix revealed the next, narrower layer — the defining pattern of the arc):**
1. **Funding (402)** — Claude account was empty; calls died at auth ($0 billed). Operator funded it. (§51.11.33)
2. **Host sleep** — the dev Mac suspended on idle/battery, freezing the container + severing live connections. Fixed via *plug-in + "prevent sleep on power adapter" toggle + caffeinate* (NOT a slice — a power setting). Chronos honestly refused to count slept time throughout.
3. **Aegis session-token expiry (Slice 220)** — THE root cause of the `AegisClientError` storm that looked like a socket bug. The Aegis session token TTL defaults to **3600s (1h)**; the bootstrap PSK is single-use; no `/session/refresh` endpoint exists. After 1h every Claude call fails `403 psk_already_consumed` until container restart. **Verify-first killed the plan's "session factory + pool reconnect"** (the HTTP session already self-heals via `_ensure_http`; the failure was a 403, not a dead socket). Fix = the codebase's own prescribed knob: `JARVIS_AEGIS_SESSION_TOKEN_TTL_S=7776000` (90d). DURABLE follow-on documented: build the real `/session/refresh` endpoint.
4. **Stale ledger hostage (Slice 217 + 221)** — `GOAL-001::file-00` sat `emitted` for hours because `goal_decomposition_ledger.jsonl` (a Jun-10 DRY-RUN-era record, pre-router-wire) said "already emitted" for an emission that never ingested → the orchestrator never re-emitted. **Slice 217** root-caused `GLS._intake_router` was NEVER assigned (the 5th cut wire) → emit went to a dry-run void; fix = one guarded line in `IntakeLayerService.start()`. **Slice 221** found the *sibling* stale ledger S217 missed. Fix = archive both + clean rebuild → fresh emit returned `emitted=True, idempotency_key=enqueued`.
5. **Sensor self-DDoS (Slices 222 + 223)** — the TestFailure sensor fired every ~30s on the SAME 3 known-pre-existing failing tests (`bg_readonly_cascade`, bisected identical on clean main), spawning IMMEDIATE ops that saturated the 3-worker pool + burned Claude on the *human-reflex lane* — starving GOAL-001 (priority 4) for 40 min. **222** = quiet the timer (config). **223** = the durable structural fix, generalizing the proven **Slice-10A pattern** (SWE-Bench fixtures once burned 99.83% of spend on Claude via the same `test_failure→IMMEDIATE→Claude-direct` masquerade): new **Priority 0.75** in `urgency_router.classify` — when `JARVIS_SOAK_SENSOR_DEMOTION_ENABLED + OUROBOROS_BATTLE_HEADLESS`, `test_failure`-source ops route STANDARD (DW primary, Claude rescue preserved). Source-discriminated (S208-safe: not a self-elevatable priority label); interactive sessions byte-identical.

**THE MONEY ANSWER (audited, not estimated):** the operator felt "$26 burned fast." The Aegis spend WAL — every call `admit→reserve→reconcile` with usage-reconciled `actual_cost_usd` — proves the **soak's total lifetime Claude spend was ~$1.90** across 821 calls ($1.44 of it the IMMEDIATE noise, now demoted). The remaining ~$24 went **outside the soak's audit trail** — prime suspect: a shared `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` on `jarvis-cloud` (Vercel) or another surface. **Action item: isolate a dedicated soak key + check the Anthropic console's by-key/by-date breakdown** (spend during the 402/token-dead eras was categorically not the soak).

**SLICE 224 — TOKEN-ECONOMIC ACCOUNTING FABRIC (the cost stack, completed):**
- **P2a prompt-prefix cache — COMPLETED, not rebuilt.** Verify-first: the builder logic existed + was proven (7 green tests incl. divert/fold/fallback) but NO call-site ever passed `stable_prefix_out` (the suite's own `on_without_sink_falls_back` documented the gap). 3 edits closed it: `generate()` → `_assemble_codegen_prompt` → fold the tool-catalog + output-schema into the CACHED system blocks (Phase-3a ephemeral `cache_control`). Cached input bills at **0.1× ($0.30/M vs $3/M) on hits**. Gated `JARVIS_PROMPT_PREFIX_CACHE_ENABLED` (default-FALSE, OFF byte-identical).
- **`accounting_ledger.py` + `/spend` REPL verb + host-side CLI** — day × provider × route rollups over the Aegis spend WAL (+ rotation backups, garbage-tolerant, NEVER raises). Provider attribution is an op-id HEURISTIC, **labeled `(inferred)`** — consoles stay authoritative (the $26 lesson institutionalized). The CLI works against a *dead* container's bind-mount.
- **`JARVIS_AEGIS_HOURLY_BURN_CAP_USD=2.00`** pinned — the burn-RATE rail (Aegis denies premium dispatch past the rate; the session cap alone couldn't stop a restart-loop compounding).

**VERIFY-FIRST CLOSED BLIND-SPOTS (code-confirmed):** (a) the Aegis reconcile parses `cache_creation_input_tokens` + `cache_read_input_tokens` (`forwarding.py:241`) → `/spend` won't drift from the console under P2a; (b) the bandit reward already includes `JARVIS_BANDIT_W_COST=0.3` (cost-aware Thompson sampling — MixLLM-class); (c) the P2a prefix is computed-once (stable, no per-op drift).

**HONEST COST VERDICT:** the demotion (223) eliminated ~75% of historical burn at the source; P2a is armed + meter-aware but **UNMEASURED** (the quiet, noise-demoted boot made 0 Claude calls — burned ≈ $0). The cost stack is now **elite and effectively complete**: metered (Aegis WAL), attributed (`/spend`), rate-capped ($2/h), cache-armed (P2a), noise-shielded (223), cost-aware-routed (bandit). A 2026 research deep-dive confirmed the architecture independently implements **FrugalGPT's cascade + cost-aware-bandit** ahead of being asked.

**THE BLUNT TRUTH THE ARC SURFACED:** quieting the noise gave GOAL-001 a clear worker pool — and `file-00` STILL did NOT dispatch (`done=0`, IMMEDIATE ops=0). **The cost work, though excellent, did NOT unblock the goal.** The real unsolved question is non-economic: *why does a funded, attested, awake, quiet organism still not dispatch its own enqueued strategic sub-goal?*

### §51.11.34-ROADMAP — Next-Slices Priority Stack (2026-06-12)

**Tier A — THE AUTONOMY BLOCKER (do first; not a cost question):**
- **A1. Trace `file-00` enqueued→dispatched.** With a clear pool it still won't move. Suspect chain: the roadmap envelope reaches `dispatch_queue` but the dequeuer (`UnifiedIntakeRouter._dispatch_loop` → `GLS.submit`) either never pulls it, or `IntakeLayerService` isn't fully booting in `--production-soak --headless` (zero `IntakeLayerService booted` lines observed in stdout — verify against the in-container `debug.log`, the authoritative sink). **This is the single highest-value next action — the milestone (first autonomous PR) is gated on it, nothing else.**

  > **A1 STATUS (2026-06-21) — DIAGNOSIS DONE; DLQ MERGED; T2–T5 SPECIFIED-NOT-BUILT.** Two converging traces + direct grep resolved the root cause (do **not** re-diagnose): the dispatch *pipe works* (`IntakeLayerService` boots + `UnifiedIntakeRouter.start()` spawns `_dispatch_loop` + `GLS.submit` reachable). The "zero `IntakeLayerService booted` lines" was a **red herring** — `silent_boot` sends INFO→`debug.log`. The real blockers: **(a)** the strategic-GOAL *source* `_roadmap_ignition_daemon` is default-OFF (`JARVIS_ROADMAP_ORCHESTRATOR_ENABLED`; set `"1"` in `docker-compose.dw-cortex-soak.yml:251` — the A1 soak venue); **(b)** a **silent-drop race** — `roadmap_orchestrator._TeeRouter.ingest()` with `upstream=None` captured the envelope and returned `"captured"` with no log/persistence. **A1-T1 fixed (b) + merged standalone:** `intake_dlq.py` (`append_dlq`/`read_dlq`/`replay_dlq`, `.jarvis/intake_dlq.jsonl`, `JARVIS_INTAKE_DLQ_ENABLED` default-true) + `_TeeRouter` None-upstream→loud+DLQ. **Remaining (full TDD code in `docs/superpowers/{specs,plans}/2026-06-21-a1-event-driven-intake-dlq-*`):** T2 event-driven router-ready valve (`intake.router.ready`, subscribe-then-check, no poll); T3 DAG-weight tag (`is_heavy_goal`→Epistemic-Matrix prefetch); T4 `[A1Trace]` WARNING breadcrumbs at 5 hops (emit→ingest→dequeue→submit→accept — the 5 ordered stdout lines ARE the proof); T5 integration. **Backpressure Health Gate DEFERRED** until a soak proves the pipe flows (admission control on a not-yet-flowing pipe masks the fix). **Proof = operator `--production-soak` on a real host (C2)** with the roadmap orchestrator on — not runnable nested on the dev Mac. Composite stays ~35% until that soak yields reviewed autonomous PRs.
- **A2. QoS reserved-slot scheduler (S221 blueprint, build-gated on A1).** Partition the worker pool: Class-0 (sensor/health noise) vs Class-1 (operator-signed roadmap targets, un-starvable reserved slots). `intake_priority_queue` already has priority buckets + a reserved-slot starvation guard; the gap is per-CLASS worker *reservation*. Build ONLY if A1 shows starvation persists with noise quieted.

**Tier B — TOKEN-ECONOMIC FOLLOW-ONS (research-backed; clear ROI, not urgent):**
- **B1. Claude Batch API for non-deadline ops (50% discount, STACKS with P2a → 95%+).** DW already uses batch transport; Claude is called synchronously. Route BACKGROUND/SPECULATIVE strategic Claude ops to the batch endpoint. *Highest-ROI unbuilt cost optimization* ([Anthropic batch+caching stacking](https://www.dotzlaw.com/insights/obsidian-notes-02/)).
- **B2. Prompt compression on VOLATILE blocks (LLMLingua line, 2-5× shrink).** P2a caches the fixed blocks; compression shrinks the variable ones (file contents, tool results). The natural successor — genuinely missing ([Pay for Hints, arXiv:2601.22132](https://arxiv.org/html/2601.22132)).
- **B3. Answer-quality cascade calibration (UCCI, arXiv:2605.18796).** The cortex has Brier self-calibration but for *rupture forecasting*, not *answer-quality confidence*. A quality-confidence layer tightens the DW→Claude escalation — where UCCI shows cascades leak money. Frontier, highest-effort.

**Tier C — DURABLE INFRA HARDENING (the temporary fixes' permanent forms):**
- **C1. Aegis `/session/refresh` endpoint** — make the token self-heal beyond ANY TTL (the real "Slice-3" the code keeps referencing; the 90d TTL is a stopgap).
- **C2. Always-on non-sleeping host** — the dev Mac is the wrong soak venue (sleep/battery flapping corrupted every measurement). A ~$10-100/mo CPU-only VPS/VM (NOT the $510/mo J-Prime L4 GPU — operator-confirmed 29× more expensive than DW for a 7B model). Migration tooling ready (`migrate_to_host.sh`).

**HONEST META (unchanged ~35% North-Star composite):** this arc moved *reliability + cost legibility*, not autonomy or evidence. The grade still gates on runtime + a reviewed autonomous-PR track record — and A1 is the precise next unlock for the first PR. Cost is solved; *completion* is not.

### §51.11.35 — Execution-Frontier + Split-Brain-Safety Arc (2026-06-21, 3 PRs merged to main: #69637 / #69638 / #69639)

**What landed (true code state, syncing the PRD past the §3.11 ignition):**

1. **Sovereign Epistemic Context Matrix — Phase 1 (PR #69637, on `main`).** Cures the **7th-layer `tool_loop_deadline_exceeded`** — heavy multi-file GOALs blowing the generation deadline because Venom re-explores the codebase from scratch every op. Fix collapses exploration from O(N) blind search to directed retrieval: an oracle-seeded **prefetch DAG** (`epistemic_prefetch.py`, reusing `oracle.get_fused_neighborhood`) seeds Venom; an **Information-Gain Governor** (`context_governor.py`) converges exploration on TF-cosine Δ-decay (sub-ms, no model call) with prefetch as the round-0 baseline + a **one-shot Iron-Gate deadlock breaker** (`deadlock_override_failed`, non-retryable); a **cryptographic session-bound Truth-Guard** (`epistemic_quarantine.py`, reusing `state_drift` sha256) drops+quarantines stale memory at consume-time. ~65 tests; cage-preserving (memory seeds exploration, never bypasses the Iron Gate's live reads). Phase 2 (ActionOutcomeMemory → GENERATE) deferred.

2. **Sovereign Async Yield Matrix — Layer 1 (PR #69638, default-ON).** Makes the *existing* Sovereign Execution Boundary (§ Slices 257/258, PRs #69533/#69534) **self-enforcing**, fixing the split-brain where the autonomous loop wrote generative mutations directly into the **primary host checkout** (because `JARVIS_FILE_ISOLATION_ENABLED` was default-OFF and nothing turned it on — *a static default is a safety vulnerability*). A **deterministic lock** (`autonomous_workspace.resolve_loop_project_root`) detects the primary checkout via `git rev-parse` and **force-arms BOTH isolation + commit-denial flags even when explicitly false**, routing to a worktree; a **raw-write guard** (`tool_executor` policy Rule 0e) denies autonomous `edit_file`/`write_file` to the primary checkout (the *actual* incident vector — previously only commits were denied). `verify_file_isolation.py --prove-override` proves the override. Deterministic, not probabilistic (Watchdog Isolation Invariant).

3. **Async Yield Matrix — Layer 2 (PR #69639, default-OFF).** Graceful operator-yield: a deterministic operator-presence detector publishes `operator.active/idle` on the `TrinityEventBus`; the `SensorGovernor` hard-zeros new-op admission; the in-flight op **cooperatively parks at its next safe checkpoint** (reusing `op_park_store`) after a **mutation critical-section drain** (`mutation_critical_section.py`) guarantees it is never parked mid-write; resumes on idle. Activated via the Daemon-Injection protocol (non-blocking watcher + governor DI + REPL input hook). ~180 tests; default-off byte-identical.

**Honest scoring — composite UNCHANGED at ~35%.** Per §51's own framing, the bottleneck is the hard 85% (proven runtime + a reviewed autonomous-PR track record + ~12–18 months of shadow evidence + the operator's Layer-4 decision), **not** engineering. This arc shipped capability the roadmap files under "the easy ~15%" (the heavy-GOAL deadline cure) + the safety substrate (deterministic isolation). It did **not** move autonomy or evidence, so the number does not move.

**What it *did* unblock (secondary but real):** two preconditions for the evidence phase the roadmap demands. (a) You cannot run a 12–18-month unattended shadow soak if the loop trashes the operator's working tree — Layer 1 isolation (live, default-on) makes sustained unattended operation *safe*, a hard precondition for **starting the evidence clock**. (b) Heavy multi-file GOALs would have failed that soak on the deadline — the Epistemic Matrix is the cure (built, **soak-unproven**). So C2 (a real non-sleeping soak host) is now *safe to run*, and its ops are now *capable of completing*.

**Unchanged gates (do not let the merge volume obscure this):**
- **A1 (trace `file-00` enqueued→dispatched) remains the named #1 autonomy gate, untouched by this arc.** The first *autonomous code-change PR via the full FSM* is still gated on it. (The graduation crucible's #69632 is an autonomous *flag-flip* PR — a narrower milestone than A1's arbitrary-roadmap-GOAL dispatch.)
- **Everything in this arc was built by the human-directed dev process (subagent-driven-development), NOT by O+V autonomously.** "Where does O+V stand execution-wise" measures O+V's *own* autonomous execution — which remains the unproven frontier. The scaffolding got materially better; the demonstration has not happened.

**Net:** the execution *ceiling* is now structurally addressed (deadline cure + safe continuous operation, both on `main`); the execution *track record* is still the frontier, gated on a soak on a real host (C2) that produces the autonomous-PR evidence. The honest "you are here" is unchanged at ~35% — but the next ~%-moving action (the soak) is now both *safe* and *capable* in a way it was not before this arc.

### §51.11.C — North Star Galaxy: Position & Honest Percentage (post-arc, 2026-06-06)

The §51.7 Tier-1→5 roadmap, re-scored against the live tree after Slices 101→119:

| Tier | Goal | Status |
|---|---|---|
| **T1** | Wire Bucket A (cognitive substrate) | ✅ **CLOSED** (Slice 101 arc; the organism drained its own backlog) |
| **T2** | §43 cage arcs + recursion bound (out-of-process containment) | ✅ **CLOSED** (104–108 Docker/seccomp containment + recursion-depth gate; 115/118 falsification-proved the cage + egress) |
| **T3** | Wire + graduate M10 (the Order-2 driver) | 🟡 **WIRED, not graduated** (Slice 119 — M10 has a bounded live-path ref; live synthesis + graduation are gated-off pending operator soak) |
| **T4** | Operator-only Layer-4 signed-roadmap authority | 🟡 **MECHANISM BUILT, decision pending** (Slice 120 — HMAC-verified signed-roadmap reader + the **un-signable safety floor** + bounded budget/recursion clamps + fail-closed-to-per-PR-review, 21 tests; the operator's standing signed-authority is the one remaining act, by design) |
| **T5** | Evidence (12–18 mo wall-clock) | 🔴 **CLOCK AT ~0** (the dissertation_evidence ledger exists + the siege accrues receipts, but the multi-month soak has not run) |

**Two-axis honest read (the percentages are calibrated judgment per §51.9, NOT measured facts):**
- **Engineering / mechanism substrate: ~90 %** (was ~10–15 % at the §51 audit baseline). The two Tier-D hurdles are closed, Second-Order RSI is wired-but-bounded, and the adversarial proving ground + cryptographic evidence harness exist. The remaining ~10 % is live-M10-synthesis wiring + the unwired tail of Bucket-A consolidation modules.
- **Evidence / authorization phase: ~5 %.** The 12–18 month wall-clock clock (T5) has barely started; the operator's signed-roadmap authority (T4) is built but unexercised.

**Overall to the fully-realized North Star: ~30–35 %, and the bottleneck has decisively shifted.** It is no longer engineering — that is largely done. The remaining mass is the **evidence clock (a clock, not code)** and the **operator's authority decision (a human judgment, by design)**. This is exactly the §51 thesis playing out: *"engineering is the easy 15 %; safety substrate + evidence + the operator's authority decision are the real 85 %."* The safety substrate is now built AND adversarially proven; what remains is to *run the clock* and *earn the operator's signature* — fully-autonomous is still **unsafe to flip today** (the operator remains the recursion bound) and is **earned, not flipped.** The §51.1 standing research debt is materially reduced: the cage's containment and the egress/recursion bounds now carry deterministic, tamper-evident receipts — the raw data the dissertation theorems are formalized from.

---

### §51.11.32 — The DoubleWord Economic Sovereignty + Predictive Transport Arc (Slices 168–172, 2026-06-08)

*Operator-driven: "DW is the funded primary — stop cascading to expensive Claude" + two real Seb/Meryem @ Doubleword emails (a cancelled deepseek-v4-pro batch; a Nemotron 3 launch). Standing constraint: "do not fund Claude … we do not patch structural gaps with financial workarounds." Verify-first throughout; every slice PR-squash-merged to `main`.*

**The thesis.** O+V runs DoubleWord (DW) as its **funded, sovereign primary** (Tier 0) with Claude as the expensive Tier-1 fallback. The arc's animating defect: DW kept **cascading to Claude on its own failure modes**, silently overspending and defeating vendor sovereignty. Five slices close the loop from *quirk-tolerance* → *reactive failover* → *visible economics* → *predictive anticipation*.

**The DW provider quirks (verified, load-bearing — `doubleword_provider.py`):**
- **`reasoning_effort: "none"` is REJECTED by some models** (deepseek-v4-pro → DW *cancels the batch*, surfaced **asynchronously** so it reads as a transport failure, not a synchronous 400). We derive `none` for trivial/simple ops, so a trivial op routed there silently cancelled → cascade.
- **High `reasoning_effort` RUPTURES the SSE chunked stream** (`ClientPayloadError: TransferEncodingError`); the dispatch *mislabels it `live_transport`*. `none/low/medium` stream cleanly. Streaming ceiling clamped to `medium` (`_dw_max_reasoning_effort`, env `JARVIS_DW_MAX_REASONING_EFFORT`).

| Slice | Title | Layer | Core mechanism | Default |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| **168** | Per-model reasoning_effort floor | Quirk-tolerance | `_dw_model_min_effort(model)` clamps effort UP to a per-model minimum (env `JARVIS_DW_MODEL_MIN_EFFORT="substr:effort"`, generic substring match — no hardcoded model in the algorithm; default `deepseek-v4-pro:low`). `_clamp_up_to_min` is the symmetric partner to `_clamp_reasoning_effort`. Threaded `model=_effective_model` at all 3 request-build sites; floors even an explicit effort. | ON |
| **169** | Dynamic capability resolver | Quirk-tolerance | `dw_catalog_client.parse_supported_reasoning_efforts` + `catalog_min_reasoning_effort` read per-model supported efforts from DW's `/v1/models` metadata (via the existing disk-cached catalog). `_dw_model_min_effort` resolves DYNAMIC-first → static-fallback (168) → `none`. Self-resolves with zero static map once DW exposes the field; byte-identical until then. | ON |
| **170** | Intra-DW transport failover | **Reactive** | **THE cost-cascade fix.** Root cause: `_slice36_should_force_batch` had `if not _claude_unavailable: return False` — DW only failed over to its OWN batch transport when **Claude was DEAD**, so a DW *stream rupture* (transport-specific) cascaded to expensive Claude whenever Claude had credit. Fix: consult the existing `_slice41_ledger_force_batch()` signal (surface-health: `DIRECT_STREAMING` degraded ∧ `BATCH_STORAGE` healthy) **BEFORE** the Claude-availability gate → force DW-batch even when Claude is available; a rupture fails over WITHIN DW. Claude stays the fallback for genuine DW-*wide* outages. `JARVIS_DW_INTRA_TRANSPORT_FAILOVER_ENABLED`, failure-path-only. | ON |
| **171** | Economic telemetry | **Observe** | `economic_telemetry.py`: thread-safe `EconomicTelemetry` singleton (intra_failover count + estimated capital saved; **832 ns/record**, lock+increment, no I/O/GIL stall). Attribution with ZERO re-eval: `force_batch=True` while Claude is AVAILABLE ⟹ the Slice 170 reroute fired (legacy batch path REQUIRES Claude unavailable) = a cascade avoided. `discord_gateway` renders a `💸 sovereignty` field on every gate embed. | ON |
| **172** | DW failure-risk predictor | **Predictive** | `dw_failure_predictor.py`: pure-Python **recency-weighted Poisson interval estimator** (no torch/tf). Rupture events land in a bounded monotonic-timestamp ring (fed UNCONDITIONALLY at `_note_dw_live_transport_degraded` — the same stream the ledger ingests); half-life-decayed weights give rate `λ`, then `P(≥1 rupture in horizon) = 1 - exp(-λ·horizon)` ∈ [0,1]. `_slice36_should_force_batch` gains a PREDICTIVE branch AFTER the reactive one: forecast ≥ threshold → preempt to batch BEFORE the stream breaks. `🔮 forecast` Discord field. Proven: cold 0.0 → 4-rupture cluster 0.865 (preempt) → decayed 0.061. | **OFF** (§33.1 — acts on a forecast) |

**The transport matrix — a complete sense → forecast → act → show loop:**
```
rupture event ─► _note_dw_live_transport_degraded
                   ├─► surface-health ledger (reactive verdict)         [170]
                   ├─► dw_transport_recovery (adaptive exp-backoff)       [127]
                   └─► dw_failure_predictor.record_rupture()              [172]
                                 │ Poisson forecast
_slice36_should_force_batch():   ▼
  1. stream CONFIRMED degraded?  → batch   (reactive, 170)
  2. forecast ≥ threshold?       → batch   (PREEMPTIVE, 172)
  3. Claude-availability fallthrough (legacy)
                                 │ a preempt is still force_batch
                                 ▼
  Discord spine:  💸 capital saved (171)  +  🔮 rupture risk % (172)
```

**Honest reliability framing (the operator's verify-first standard).** This arc does **not** make DW *internally* more reliable — DW's streaming wire still ruptures. It makes O+V's *use* of DW more **resilient**: it tolerates DW's param quirks (168/169), routes around its known transport failure mode within DW instead of cascading (170), makes the savings auditable (171), and anticipates the failure to dodge it pre-emptively (172). DW becomes a more reliable *effective* primary through intelligent routing, not through any change to DW.

**Known blindspots (explicitly deferred, not silently ignored):**
- **(A) No batch-health guard on the predictive (172) branch** — ✅ **CLOSED (Slice 173, the Multi-Surface Safety Guard).** The predictive detour now fires only if the rupture forecast is high AND `BATCH_STORAGE` is `HEALTHY` (via `_dw_batch_lane_healthy`, reusing the existing `preflight_probe._batch_surface_healthy` ledger check — no duplication, fails closed). If the stream is risky but batch is also degraded, the detour aborts and the op stays on RT → a subsequent rupture correctly cascades to Claude (both DW surfaces compromised). Proven against a seeded ledger.
- **(B) Global, not per-model, rupture rate** — one forecast for all DW models; Qwen3.5-397B / DeepSeek-V4-Pro / Nemotron-3 rupture at different rates. A per-model ring would route the rupture-prone model to batch while keeping a stable one on RT.
- **(C) Open-loop** — no prediction-accuracy (Brier/calibration) feedback; the 0.7 threshold is fixed, not self-tuned against observed hit/miss.
- **(D) Single-failure-mode coverage** — 172 forecasts *transport ruptures* only. Not modelled: batch-lane failures, `UPSTREAM_DEGRADED`/`done_before_content`, param-rejection batch-cancels (the 168 class), or economic/quota `402/429` (the circuit breaker's domain).

**Nemotron 3 (Super-120B / Meryem's "Ultra") — candidate fit for O+V:** an agentic reasoning model (256K context, "5× throughput / 30% lower cost-to-task on SWE-bench" per DW) → fits the **COMPLEX/heavy_code route**, the **Venom multi-turn tool loop**, the **PLAN phase**, and **L3 subagents** (long-horizon agentic reasoning + large context). Integration is policy-driven (`brain_selection_policy.yaml` + dw_catalog — no hardcoded model), the 169 resolver handles its effort capabilities, and the 30%-cost claim is **directly A/B-testable on the SWE-Bench-Pro soak**. Precondition: confirm its `reasoning_effort: none` support (open question to Seb) so it doesn't re-trigger the 168 batch-cancel class.

---

### §51.11.33 — The Predictive Cortex Hardening Arc (Slices 173–174, 2026-06-08)

*Operator-driven, immediately after §51.11.32: "we do not leave known correctness gaps in production" (Blindspot A) + "an intelligent cortex that relies on a hand-coded open-loop threshold is functionally stagnant and violates the no-hardcoding directive" (Blindspot C). Closes two of the four §51.11.32 blindspots.*

**Slice 173 — Multi-Surface Safety Guard (closes Blindspot A, a *correctness* gap).** Slice 172's predictive branch preempted to batch on a rupture forecast *without* verifying the batch lane was healthy — so a forecast could detour an op INTO a degraded batch lane. Fix: the detour now fires only if the forecast is high **AND** `BATCH_STORAGE` is `HEALTHY`, via `_dw_batch_lane_healthy()` — which **reuses the existing** `preflight_probe._batch_surface_healthy()` ledger check (no duplicate health logic, fails closed). The verified-detour matrix: *low risk* → RT; *high risk ∧ batch healthy* → preempt to batch; *high risk ∧ batch degraded* → **abort detour, stay RT** → a subsequent rupture correctly cascades to Claude (both DW surfaces compromised = the one case Claude *should* catch). Proven against a seeded ledger.

**Slice 174 — Cognitive Self-Calibration Loop (closes Blindspot C, an *intelligence* gap).** The Slice 172 threshold was a fixed `0.7`. Slice 174 makes it self-tuning: `dw_failure_predictor.ThresholdCalibrator` evaluates the cortex's OWN past predictions against the actual rupture record and nudges the threshold —
- **False Positive** (predicted high, the stream stayed stable through the forecast window) → **RAISE** (less trigger-happy);
- **False Negative** (predicted low, a rupture occurred in the window) → **LOWER** (more aggressive);

bounded `[JARVIS_DW_CALIBRATION_THRESHOLD_FLOOR=0.30, _CEILING=0.95]`, step `JARVIS_DW_CALIBRATION_STEP=0.02`. A **Brier score** (`mean (p−outcome)²`) is tracked as the quality metric. The calibrated threshold **PERSISTS to the host `.jarvis` volume** (`dw_threshold_calibration.json`, atomic write, fail-soft) so a container restart doesn't cause amnesia — the same durability principle as the Slice 164 breaker (but persisting only the threshold float, no wall-clock TTL needed). Prediction recording is **debounced to ~one per forecast horizon** so correlated same-window routing decisions don't over-tune. The `0.7` is now an *env-seeded baseline that mutates at runtime*, not a hardcoded constant. Gated `JARVIS_DW_CALIBRATION_ENABLED` **default-FALSE** (§33.1 — new adaptive behavior; OFF = byte-identical static Slice-172 threshold). Integration: `rupture_risk_threshold()` returns the calibrator's live value when enabled; `DWFailurePredictor.risk_exceeds_threshold()` drives the evaluate→record→compare loop at each routing decision. **Proven:** 6 synthetic false-positives drove `0.50 → 0.80`; 6 false-negatives drove `0.70 → 0.40`.

**Blindspot ledger after this arc:** **(A) ✅ CLOSED (173)** · **(C) ✅ CLOSED (174)** · **(B) ✅ CLOSED (175)** · **(D) ✅ CLOSED (176)**. ALL FOUR blindspots closed. The cortex is now *correct* (won't detour into a broken lane), *adaptive* (tunes its own decision boundary), *granular* (per-model awareness), and *omniscient* (fuses the full failure spectrum).

**Slice 176 — Multi-Signal Failure Predictor (closes Blindspot D).** The cortex (172-175) forecast from TRANSPORT ruptures ONLY — blind to ~80% of DW's failure spectrum. Slice 176 fuses the full taxonomy: each per-model ring stores `(timestamp, KIND)` events, and the risk score is a **severity-weighted Poisson rate** `λ = Σ weight(kind)·decay(age)`. Vectors + default weights (env-tunable `JARVIS_DW_SIGNAL_WEIGHT_<KIND>`): `transport` 1.0 (SSE rupture, baseline), `economic` 2.0 (402/429 quota — HIGH, imminent total lockdown), `upstream` 0.4 (empty/malformed/5xx — localized, low), `cancel` 0.6 (batch param-rejection, Slice 168 class). So a quota lockdown drives risk far faster than a localized empty completion. `record_failure(now, model_id, kind)` is the generic recorder; `record_rupture` is the transport wrapper (so a transport-only ring is **byte-identical to Slice 172** — weight 1.0 == unweighted). Wiring leverages the existing `FailureSource` taxonomy: `candidate_generator._record_dw_failure_signal` maps `LIVE_HTTP_429→economic`, `LIVE_HTTP_5XX/PARSE→upstream`, `LIVE_STREAM_STALL→transport` at the central dispatch-failure handler (transport ruptures still fed via `_note_dw_live_transport_degraded`). The self-calibrating Brier engine (174) evaluates against failure OCCURRENCE (any vector = a positive outcome). `dominant_signal(model_id)` reports the vector driving the level; the Discord spine shows it (`… · via economic`). **Proven:** 2 economic events → risk `0.865` (above threshold) while 2 upstream events → `0.330` (stays low); per-model isolation preserved (an economic storm on deepseek leaves qwen at `0.0`).

**Slice 175 — Multi-Model Tracking Ring (closes Blindspot B).** The Slice 172/174 ring + calibrator were GLOBAL — a volatile model's ruptures raised a stable model's forecast (and a stable model's stability lowered a volatile one's). Slice 175 decentralizes the cortex: `DWFailurePredictor` keeps an **independent rupture-timestamp ring per DW model** (`_rings: {model_key → deque}`, case-normalized key, `""` = the isolated unknown bucket), and `get_threshold_calibrator(model_id)` returns a **distinct self-tuning calibrator + persist file per model** (`dw_threshold_calibration_<model>.json`). `record_rupture(now, model_id)` is fed the model at the rupture-detection point (`_note_dw_live_transport_degraded`, where `model_id` was already in the diagnostic string); `_slice36_should_force_batch(context, *, model_id=_effective_model)` queries the target model's OWN forecast at the DW dispatch site; `risk_exceeds_threshold(now, model_id)` drives that model's calibration loop. The Discord spine shows the **riskiest model** + its own threshold (`highest_risk_model()`), not a misleading global average. **Proven (cross-contamination eliminated):** flooding `deepseek-v4-pro` with 5 ruptures → its forecast `0.918` (→ BATCH) while `qwen3.5-397b` stays `0.000` (→ STREAMS, unpenalized). Backward-compatible: callers without a model use the shared `""` bucket. 9 tests.

| 2026-04-27 | 2.58 | **Phase 9.1c — Fix A: post-asyncio teardown watchdog arming — closes the shutdown-hang root cause from the once-run.** Per the empirical Option-B once-run (session `bt-2026-04-27-085300`): `_generate_report` completed cleanly at 02:09:25, but the Python process never exited; sat for 1h 50m+ in `loop.shutdown_default_executor()` waiting on a non-daemon ThreadPoolExecutor worker. **Root cause** (diagnosed in Fix A): `BoundedShutdownWatchdog` (Harness Epic Slice 1) WAS already in place — but only armed in the harness's signal-handler path (`harness.py:3276`, gated on `signal_name is not None`). Clean shutdowns (`idle_timeout` / `budget_exhausted` / `wall_clock_cap`) skip the arming and have NO escape hatch when the post-asyncio teardown phase wedges on a non-daemon executor worker. **Fix A (this PR, ~25 LOC + 8 pins)**: arms the watchdog at the START of `main()`'s `finally` block in `scripts/ouroboros_battle_test.py`, BEFORE `loop.shutdown_asyncgens()`, regardless of stop_reason. Reason="post_asyncio_teardown"; deadline=`default_deadline_s()` (30s default, env-tunable via `JARVIS_BATTLE_SHUTDOWN_DEADLINE_S`). Watchdog's first-arm-wins semantics reset on disarm — the signal-handler arm-then-disarm sequence doesn't block a subsequent re-arm. Daemon-thread design (per Slice 1 spec) means no `Py_FinalizeEx` interference: if shutdown wedges past deadline, `os._exit(75)` (`EXIT_CODE_HARNESS_WEDGED`) fires; if everything completes cleanly, the daemon thread dies with the interpreter — no `os._exit` fires. **Defensive belt-and-suspenders**: arm() wrapped in try/except so a watchdog raise can't block clean exit. **8 new regression pins** (`tests/battle_test/test_post_asyncio_watchdog_arming.py`): 3 source-level pins (`reason="post_asyncio_teardown"` literal present + arm BEFORE shutdown_asyncgens + arm in try/except) + 3 watchdog behavior pins (fires-when-wedged / does-not-fire-when-disarmed-in-time / re-arms-cleanly-after-signal-handler-disarm) + 2 default-deadline-s pins (env-override + 30s-default). **Combined regression: 339/339 green** (8 new Fix A + 23 existing BoundedShutdownWatchdog + 308 Phase 9 + Item #4 + cron installer). **Cron-readiness impact**: combined with Fix B (PR #24719's breadcrumb persistence), the cron now has BOTH a forensic trail per soak (Bug #2 closed) AND a deadline escape hatch on shutdown wedge (Bug #1 closed). The two outstanding once-run blockers are NOW BOTH addressed. **Bug #3 — 0-op session pattern (BG-starvation)** remains separate; harness behavior is correct (P9.2 GraduationContract correctly classifies 0-op sessions as RUNNER); the underlying BG-starvation root cause is documented in `memory/project_wave3_item6_graduation_matrix.md` (F3 side-arc) and is out of scope for the cron-install path. **PRD updated**: Doc History v2.58 (append-only). **Path to running cadence**: with Fix A + Fix B landed, a re-run of `bash scripts/install_live_fire_soak_cron.sh --once` should now (a) complete cleanly OR (b) fire `os._exit(75)` after 30s wedge — either way the cron survives. Then `--install` is safe to commit. | Claude Opus 4.7 (Phase 9.1c — Fix A post-asyncio watchdog arming; closes shutdown-hang root cause) |
| 2026-04-27 | 2.57 | **Phase 9.1b — Fix B: breadcrumb persistence + INTERRUPTED status — closes a real bug surfaced by the once-run.** Per the empirical Option-B once-run (PRD post-mortem session `bt-2026-04-27-085300`): the harness wrote `summary.json` cleanly at 02:09:25 but the Python process never exited (atexit/asyncio shutdown hang); when the harness CLI was eventually externally killed (SIGTERM), **NO evidence row landed on disk** because persistence happened only AFTER `subprocess.run` returned successfully. The cron would have jammed every 8 hours with hung Pythons + zero evidence to grep — invisible failure mode. **Fix B (this PR, ~80 LOC + 5 pins)**: refactors `LiveFireSoakHarness.run_soak` to write a **breadcrumb evidence row BEFORE the runner is invoked** (status `SUBPROCESS_IN_FLIGHT`) and wraps the subprocess invocation in a `try/except BaseException` block that catches `SystemExit` / `KeyboardInterrupt` (SIGTERM-induced), persists an `INTERRUPTED` row, and re-raises so the caller's signal propagates cleanly. **2 new HarnessStatus enum values**: `SUBPROCESS_IN_FLIGHT` (breadcrumb — paired with completion row by session_id; lone breadcrumb on disk = hung soak) + `INTERRUPTED` (caught BaseException mid-subprocess; persisted with outcome=infra so the flag's clean-count is NOT blocked by harness-internal hangs). **Persistence ordering**: breadcrumb hits disk via `_append_history_row` BEFORE `runner(...)` returns — proven by `test_breadcrumb_written_before_subprocess_returns` which has the runner stub read `.jarvis/live_fire_graduation_history.jsonl` mid-invocation and assert the breadcrumb is already there. **Defensive belt-and-suspenders**: the BaseException handler's own `_persist_failure` call is wrapped in a last-ditch `try/except Exception` so even a persistence-side raise won't block SystemExit propagation (the cron MUST be able to terminate cleanly when the operator kills it). **Authority posture preserved**: still NEVER raises `Exception` into caller; BaseException re-raises after evidence row written; lazy substrate imports unchanged; AST-pinned cage invariants survive. **5 new regression pins** (`tests/governance/test_p9_1_live_fire_soak.py`) covering: breadcrumb-written-before-runner-returns (load-bearing — proves the disk-write-ordering invariant via runner-stub reads disk mid-call) + breadcrumb-row-correct-metadata (flag_name + session_id="in-flight" + outcome=infra + runner_attributed=False + stop_reason="subprocess_in_flight" + finished_at_iso="" empty) + INTERRUPTED-via-KeyboardInterrupt-persists-row + INTERRUPTED-via-SystemExit-persists-row (more direct SIGTERM mapping) + 2-status-values-added bit-rot pin + breadcrumb-doesnt-count-as-runner-outcome (INTERRUPTED uses outcome=infra so a hung soak doesn't unfairly block the flag's clean-count). **2 existing pins updated** for the new 2-rows-per-soak pattern: `test_evidence_persisted_to_history_jsonl` now asserts both breadcrumb + completion present + correctly distinguishes by `harness_status`; | 2026-04-26 | 2.47 | **AST Validator Rule 8 — module-level side-effect detection shipped — closes the highest-priority remaining sandbox-bypass vector.** Extends `meta/ast_phase_runner_validator.py` Slice 3 validator with a new structural check that runs BEFORE the candidate ever reaches the sandbox: walks the module's TOP-LEVEL statement list (not function/class bodies — those are Rule 7's domain) for two complementary patterns. **Pattern 1**: bare module-level `Call` (or `Assign`/`AnnAssign`/`AugAssign` whose RHS contains a Call) to a name in `_BANNED_MODULE_LEVEL_CALLS` — the banned set is built via string-concatenation in `_build_banned_module_level_calls()` (security-scan friendly) and contains shell exec (the `os` shell-and-spawn family), the `subprocess` family (Popen/run/call/check_output/check_call/getoutput/getstatusoutput), code-exec primitives (eval/exec/compile), dynamic-import primitives (the `__import__` builtin and `importlib` import_module / dunder-import), the standard Python deserialization-RCE primitives (the `p`+`ickle` family + `marshal.loads/load`), and bare `open()`. **Pattern 2**: module-level control-flow block (`if`/`for`/`while`/`with`/`try`/`AsyncFor`/`AsyncWith`/`Match` Py 3.10+) containing ANY Call — the rationale is that well-behaved candidates declare functions/classes; they don't run conditional logic at import time. Top-level docstrings (Constant str Expr), function/class defs, imports, simple Assign/AnnAssign/AugAssign (with non-banned RHS Calls — e.g. `logger = logging.getLogger(__name__)` is allowed), and `pass` are the only allowed top-level shapes. New failure reason `MODULE_LEVEL_SIDE_EFFECT` added to `ValidationFailureReason` enum (10th value; full set re-pinned via renamed `test_validation_failure_reason_ten_values`). Per-rule kill switch `JARVIS_AST_VALIDATOR_BLOCK_MODULE_SIDE_EFFECTS` defaults **TRUE** (security hardening on by default — same convention as Rule 7's `JARVIS_AST_VALIDATOR_BLOCK_INTROSPECTION_ESCAPE`); operators can disable in emergency without disabling the whole validator. New helpers `_resolve_call_name(call_node)` (Best-effort dotted-name resolution: `foo()`→"foo", `mod.foo()`→"mod.foo", `pkg.mod.foo()`→"pkg.mod.foo", returns None for `f()()` / `getattr(x, "y")()` opaque shapes) + `_has_any_call(node)` (recursive walk for any Call) + `_find_module_level_side_effect(tree)` — all stdlib `ast` only, never raise. **Known limitations pinned in tests** (not silent gaps — visible in test output): (a) **alias-defeats-resolver** — assigning a banned dotted name to a local then calling the local slips through (the alias's value-side resolves correctly but the call site only sees the local name); (b) **call-on-call** — `factory()()` opaque to the static dotted-name resolver. Both gaps are tracked as defense-in-depth gaps; Rule 7 catches `__class__`/`__bases__`/`__subclasses__` introspection in any function body, and the sandbox's limited builtin set blunts most aliases at runtime. **82 regression pins** (`tests/governance/test_ast_rule_8_module_level_side_effects.py`) covering: 1 enum-value pin + 14 kill-switch pins (default-true + 6 truthy + 6 falsy) + 17 Pattern-1 banned-name pins (parametrized across `os` shell-and-spawn + the spawn 7-suffix family + the exec 7-suffix family + `subprocess` 7-method family + eval/exec/compile + 3 dynamic-import + marshal + the `p`+`ickle` family + bare-open) + 3 RHS-shape pins (Assign + AnnAssign + nested-Call-in-list) + 7 Pattern-2 control-flow pins (if/for/while/with/try + innocuous-call-in-if + allow-if-without-call) + 6 clean-candidates-pass pins (simple-assigns + logger=getLogger + function-def + module-docstring + banned-call-inside-function-body-not-tripped + banned-call-inside-method-not-tripped) + 5 adversarial-corpus pins (alias-NOT-blocked-known-gap + call-on-call-NOT-blocked-known-gap + match-stmt-blocked Py3.10+-skipif + top-level-pass + top-level-import) + 3 per-rule kill-switch behavior pins (kill-off-passes + master-off-skips-everything + Rule-7-still-fires-when-Rule-8-off) + 7 white-box helper-direct pins (3 `_resolve_call_name` + 2 `_has_any_call` + 2 banned-set-shape-and-categories) + 3 short-circuit pins (oversize + parse-error + never-raises-on-edge-cases). Existing pin `test_validation_failure_reason_nine_values` renamed to `..._ten_values` and updated to include `MODULE_LEVEL_SIDE_EFFECT`. Combined regression spine: **137/137 AST validator tests green** (existing 56-pin suite + 81 new Rule 8 pins; 1 skipped on Py 3.9 for match-statement coverage). **🟢 Highest-priority remaining sandbox vector closed**: post-Phase-7.7, operator-approved candidates with module-level RCE-shape code at import time were the next attack class on the brutal-review priority list — Rule 8 hard-rejects those candidates BEFORE the sandbox starts. Schema invariant: output ALWAYS contains every base_weights key (preserving structure); unknown adapted keys silently dropped (Pass C cannot ADD categories — that's a Pass B Order-2 amendment). Constants: MAX_ADAPTED_REBALANCES=8 + MAX_WEIGHT_VALUE=100.0 + MIN_WEIGHT_VALUE=0.01 + HALF_OF_BASE=0.5 + MAX_YAML_BYTES=4 MiB. Per-entry hardening: weights dict with non-string keys / non-numeric / weight<=0 / empty SKIPPED; weight > MAX_WEIGHT_VALUE clamped; category keys lowercased + stripped. Latest-occurrence-wins (only LAST entry consulted — matches Slice 5 miner's "ONE rebalance per cycle" design).
